- **What:** Operational docs that still invoked component `--self-test` CLI flags as runnable commands are updated to **pytest / live smoke-tests** (commit `063fe766`): `headless-test-plan.md` Part A + results table → `pytest tests/test_*.py`; `g9-spine-plan.md`, `g10-ingest-plan.md`, `release-candidate-runbook.md` → pytest component tests; `diagnose-a-denied-write.md` → a live `--decide` gate smoke-test. **Why:** the `--self-test` flags were removed when L1 tests moved to the repo-side pytest tree (ADR-44) and the scripts now *reject* `--self-test` (verified live: all five reject it) — the docs were prescribing a command that no longer exists, a docs↔implementation contradiction. Frozen alpha.1 records and the ADRs keep their historical references intentionally.

- **What:** The `eval/` folder is clarified as `system/eval/` — gold-task fixtures for the quarterly vault-eval (diagnostic, non-gating) — and flagged as a *discoverability*, not a missing-artifact, problem; metrics dashboards (`eval-trend`/`fleet-health`) reading not-yet-existing `system/metrics/...` must show graceful "no data yet" messaging rather than an error (`tmp/ui-design-research-report.md` §5, §9 D-8). **Why:** review questions ("what are the files in the eval folder?") revealed unlabeled visible folders; the metrics-empty state is expected until cron sweeps populate it and shouldn't read as a failure.

### Security

- **What:** Reaffirms the **MCP-only sandbox** as a hard boundary in two plugin decisions: Shell Commands rejected because arbitrary OS execution violates it (ADR-72), and `cli-rest-mcp` rejected because its single generic `execute` tool "defeats the named-tool write gate" and is redundant with the existing Local REST API MCP (ADR-31) (`tmp/ui-design-research-report.md` §10). Buttons Panel skipped for its JS-exec security surface; the in-use Buttons (shabegom) plugin flagged as "our highest-risk current dependency" with an exit plan to native Bases actions / Commander. **Why:** the named-tool write gate + audit chain is the security model — a plugin exposing a generic execute escape hatch or arbitrary shell would bypass the policy MCP that every mutating vault operation must pass through (`mcp/README.md`: "Every mutating vault operation must pass through the policy MCP and complete its audit record").

- **What:** ADR-74's deferred model adds a **CI provenance doctor** requirement (lock↔artifact match, one entry per enabled plugin, no undeclared executable artifact) as a security control over the bundled plugin binaries. **Why:** currently a changed minified `main.js` cannot be traced to an upstream release — an opaque binary supply-chain gap.

### ADRs

- **ADR-69** (proposed) — Operations layer naming + four categories. Assumes ADR-46 (amends its "engine" term; ADR-46 keeps the architecture). Excludes from find/replace: the `memoria-engineer` persona, qmd's "search engine", and the `PolicyEngine` class name (decided separately). Sequenced after ADR-73.
- **ADR-70** (proposed) — Navigation gates / ambient maintenance / JTBD dashboards. Assumes 68, 69; extends ADR-68 rather than replacing it (the Studio shell becomes the alpha.4 Project gate).
- **ADR-71** (proposed) — Structured capture forms / Linter authority / one schema per type. Assumes 49, 30.
- **ADR-72** (proposed) — Command surfacing / Commander / Co-PI additive. Assumes 48.
- **ADR-73** (proposed) — Documentation references: never link into `src/` from a published page (inline-code path by default; tag-pinned `blob/<tag>` URL only when a click adds value; `docs-doctor check_site_local_links` flags violations, advisory now → promote to error after the sweep); ADR references kept out of tutorial/how-to/reference body text and subheadings (allowed only inline in explanation pages + an optional per-page "Decisions" footer, always as title-text links; bare `(D##)` codes purged as link rot); complex operations split into procedural reference + rationale explanation pages. Assumes 46, 12; sequenced **before** the ADR-69 rename so links aren't pinned to paths about to move.
- **ADR-74** (deferred) — Pinned Obsidian plugin supply-chain manifest (detailed above).
- **README index** (`docs/adr/README.md`) updated with all six one-line summaries and statuses.

- **What (ADR-73 tooling landed):** `docs-doctor` gains a `check_site_local_links` advisory flagging published docs→`src/` relative links that 404 on the Jekyll site, with a test, and the convention is documented in the docs-review skill (commit `610604f1`; grounded in `tmp/ui-design-research-report.md` §8). **Why:** the site is Jekyll + just-the-docs on GitHub Pages where `src/` is a *sibling* of the `docs/` source root and thus never published — so *every* relative link from a docs page into `src/` breaks on the live site regardless of depth, and the earlier "✓ works" verdicts were filesystem checks that pass lint while the link is dead on the website (§8 "Grounding"). Currently ~77 advisories across ~70 links in 17 files; exit stays 0 (advisory) so CI is unaffected until the sweep + promotion to error (issue #464).

### Issue-tracking system (release/process design — the version's headline focus)

- **What:** A new **GitHub-Project-based issue-tracking model** is documented (`docs/releasing/0.1.0-alpha.3/tmp/issue-tracking-guide.md`, commit `63751936`): planning metadata moves off labels into **Project #1 single-select fields** — **Status, Area, Type, Priority** — with milestones carrying release phase, sub-issues carrying hierarchy, and labels kept minimal. Guiding rule: "each kind of metadata lives on the feature that models it best, never duplicated." **Why:** the pre-alpha.3 tracker was label soup (`enhancement`/`question`/`research`/`needs-scoping`) that overloaded search chips with planning state; the mental model is fixed as "the issue is the work; Project fields slice it; the milestone is when; the ADR is why."

- **What:** **Status finalized to exactly five states in board order** — Backlog · In progress · In review · Done · Deferred (commit `7581edb1`); `Needs scoping` and `Blocked` were **deliberately dropped**. **Why:** option order = board column order (left = active lifecycle read as progress, right = inactive Done/Deferred); the two dropped states "each overlapped Backlog / In progress and earned no distinct action" — capture that signal with a note or Priority instead. Deferred is defined as a *revisit-each-cycle* parking lot, not a graveyard. Operational caution recorded: re-add statuses via the UI because editing field options via API can wipe existing item values.

- **What:** **Type** taxonomy (Bug/Feature/Refactor/Docs/Research/Decision) mapped from retired labels, **Area** taxonomy of 9 subsystems (capture/ingest/knowledge/obsidian-ui/operations/docs-site/installer/integrations/agents), **Priority** reserved `High` for tutorial/core-loop blockers only. The `operations` Area name explicitly matches ADR-69 (with the four categories as sub-kinds named in the issue body). **Why:** to give each work item exactly one Type/Status/Priority and one-or-more Area, filterable in the Project, while `bug`/`documentation` survive as *labels* only because repo-wide `is:issue` search and bots (Dependabot/release-please) see labels but not Project fields — the one acknowledged trade-off.

- **What:** A **Field color scheme** is specified (commit `7581edb1`): semantic fields encode meaning (Status = flow, Priority = heat), categorical fields use distinct hues as tags; reserve Red = severity/breakage, Green = good/done, Gray = neutral/inactive. Concrete assignments given for Status/Priority/Type; Sub-issues progress bar set to **Purple** ("a partial warm bar reads as a warning; purple/blue/green read as neutral progress"); Area left on auto-color (9 areas > GitHub's 8-color palette). **Why:** to make the board legible at a glance and avoid color miscues (a warm progress bar misreading as an alert).

- **What:** A **per-issue field-population map** for all 74 open issues (`tmp/project-field-mapping.md`, commit `63751936`) with bulk-pass instructions; the one-time population was executed via the API in a single scripted batch (184 edits), and retired labels (`enhancement`, `question`, `research`, `needs-scoping`) are to be deleted after Type is populated. **Why:** operationalizes the migration; documents the CLI gotchas (Projects need a project-scoped PAT via `env -u GITHUB_TOKEN`; bulk milestone/label edits across issues you didn't author are hard-blocked by the harness external-write guard, so use the table view).

### Removed / retired

- **What:** The **`_reports/` scratch-folder convention is retired** repo-wide (commit `263a2b9a`): removed from `.gitignore`, cspell, VSCode settings, `pr_policy.py` safe-prefixes, tests, `AGENTS.md`, and the alpha.3 audit doc. **Why:** `_notes/` already covers the same use-case, so `_reports/` was redundant machinery — collapsed to one scratch convention.

- **What:** The terms **"engine" and "app"** for the deterministic layer are retired at the concept level (ADR-69), and bare **`(D##)` design-note references** are marked for purge sitewide (ADR-73; `tmp/ui-design-research-report.md` §8). **Why:** "engine"/"app" is the two-words-one-concept anti-pattern; `(D##)` codes point at deleted design docs and are never link targets — pure link rot. (The engines→operations *code/doc* rename itself is scheduled, not executed in this range — the in-tree READMEs still read "Engines".)

- **What:** The copied constants and cross-module import in the MCP servers are retired: `patterns_mcp`'s local `REVIEW_GATED_PREFIXES` mirror and `tasks_mcp`'s `import policy_mcp` are deleted in favor of `memoria_runtime.policy` (commit `7b7a28ba`). **Why:** eliminate divergence risk between the gate and its consumers (see Gate section).

- **What:** Release-folder `tmp/` scratch is excluded from doc linters and Jekyll but tracked in git (commits `0d7d1712`, `_config.yml` diff adds `"**/tmp/"` to Jekyll `exclude`; docs-doctor/status-doctor/markdownlint skip `tmp/`). **Why:** the alpha.3 research reports needed to live in-repo for relative linking (and to survive as the design record) without being published or gated by linters — "tracked in git for relative linking, never published."

---

Key file references: ADRs `docs/adr/69`–`74`; research/decision sources `docs/releasing/0.1.0-alpha.3/tmp/{open-issues-research,ui-design-research-report,naming-and-diataxis-audit,alpha3-triage,issue-tracking-guide,project-field-mapping}.md`; shipped code `src/.memoria/memoria_runtime/policy/{__init__,paths}.py` + slimmed `src/.memoria/mcp/{policy_mcp,patterns_mcp,tasks_mcp}.py`; contracts `src/.memoria/{schemas,engines,profiles,mcp}/README.md`; docs updates `docs/testing/plans/*`, `docs/how-to/troubleshooting/diagnose-a-denied-write.md`, `docs/_config.yml`.

## alpha.4 — Plan-the-build checkpoint: the ExecPlan artifact, a settled packaging target, and the intent-gate PI surface

alpha.4 is an **internal checkpoint whose defining work is planning infrastructure, not shipped runtime**: it introduces the **ExecPlan** — a self-contained, resumable working document adapted from OpenAI Codex — and uses it to scope milestone #3 down to a buildable set; it settles (but defers) the runtime-as-a-wheel packaging target in ADR-76; and it lands an early wave of PI-surface polish that turns the three Obsidian workspaces into named **intent gates** (Desk / Library / Studio). The commit range `7581edb1..b1657d92` ends at the ExecPlan finalization, so the big implementation workstreams that ExecPlan describes (the `engines→operations` rename, ingest sources, native Windows) are *planned here and land in later PRs* — what actually ships in-range is the planning/ADR scaffolding plus the capture/dashboard/vocabulary improvements. Two clean-sheet design notes (an all-Linux test harness; the Project gate) were authored in this range and then deliberately pushed forward to alpha.5 as not-alpha.4 work.

---

### Planning & process (the headline change)

- **What:** Introduced the **ExecPlan** as a first-class working-document type — a new playbook (`.agents/playbooks/exec-plan.md`) + fill-in template (`.agents/templates/exec-plan.md`, 137 lines, 12 sections: Metadata → Purpose → Context → Plan → Concrete steps → Validation → Idempotence → Progress → Execution log → Surprises → Interfaces → Outcomes), registered in `.agents/README.md` with an `AGENTS.md` pointer and a new work-routing row (commit a760d0ef). **Why:** complex/multi-hour tasks had no home that survived context loss or handoff — "what was I doing and what is left" lived only in chat history. The playbook states the problem directly: a stateless agent or a novice must be able to "read it top to bottom and produce a working, observable result without asking for the next step." The approach was **adapted, not copied**, from OpenAI Codex ExecPlans and explicitly *reconciled* with three existing Memoria invariants: (a) split into playbook-vs-template to match how releases already separate the two; (b) the plan's Execution log holds only tactical/sequencing choices — architectural/product decisions still go to an ADR and are linked, preserving the ADR-only decision model; (c) an ExecPlan is a **working artifact, not a permanent record**, so instances live only in the tracked `docs/releasing/<version>/tmp/` and are deleted before the release closes (`_notes/` is gitignored and invisible to other agents, so a resumable plan can never live there) (a760d0ef commit body; `AGENTS.md` new "ExecPlans" section).

- **What:** Added the first ExecPlan instance — `docs/releasing/0.1.0-alpha.4/tmp/exec-plan-alpha.4.md` (347 lines) — inventorying all 25 open milestone-#3 issues, grouped into workstreams A–H, and recording the **2026-06-15 scope decision** (§2.2 declared authoritative) (commits 7dd0d09f, b1657d92). **Why:** the milestone was an ambiguous mix of buildable deliverables and deferred-ADR *tracking* issues; the plan's purpose is that every issue ends up "either **shipped and verifiable from the Obsidian UI** or **consciously deferred to a cadence-reviewed ADR** — with nothing left in the ambiguous middle." Honest scoping the plan surfaced: ~5 milestoned issues are pure ADR-cadence trackers (not deliverables); several PI-surface issues cite retired `docs/design/*.md` paths that must be repointed; and the full wheel migration stays deferred (only the tooling-only pyproject step is actionable) (7dd0d09f body).

- **What:** Finalized alpha.4 scope in the ExecPlan (§2.2), b1657d92. **Deferred out:** #527 HTTPS transport, #379/#559 calibration spec + score-* skills, #344 diversity reserve, #412 (ADR-62 harnesses, split to #560/#561), #370 (ADR-38 ratchet — alpha.4 keeps only shadow/report-only; enforcement → #562). **Added in:** the `engines→operations` rename (ADR-69) as a structural prerequisite (new Workstream H); #414 native Windows; #439 Mapper Tier 2; #443 contradiction-page fixes. **Why:** the 2026-06-16 revalidation against **live Hermes docs** changed the facts — Hermes now documents `ssl_verify` for HTTP/SSE MCP (unblocking #527) and native Windows support (accepting ADR-64) — so items previously deferred on missing-capability grounds became buildable, while calibration/enforcement work was split out to keep alpha.4 "free of blocked/deferred omnibus scope." The commit is careful to reframe native Windows as an **alpha.3 carry-over, not a v0.3 scope-up** (ADR-64's "revisit after alpha.3"), and flags #296's body as carrying a stale `v0.3` label to fix at source (b1657d92 second commit).

- **What:** Codified three cross-cutting **Working principles** in `AGENTS.md` (new section): *cover the whole scope* (no sampling/grep-as-read; verify sub-agent coverage), *zero tolerated contradictions* (docs must agree with each other and the implementation; sweep via the source-of-truth + change-impact maps and fix, don't log), *verify hard conclusions independently* (fresh agent + live-test the allowed/denied/fail-closed path; ground Hermes claims in `~/.hermes` docs first) (commit fcb912c9). **Why:** these rules "governed agent behavior only via one operator's private memory, not the repo" — externalizing them into the authoritative agent-policy home closes that gap. The maps are *referenced as the mechanism, not restated,* precisely to avoid the drift the zero-contradiction rule forbids. The same commit added a `.agents/playbooks/release.md` pointer to the `RELEASE_PLEASE_TOKEN` setup so the release entry point surfaces the silent-failure risk if the PAT lapses.

---

### Distribution / packaging

- **What:** Added **deferred ADR-76** — "Package the Python runtime as an installable wheel; vault holds data, not source" (`status: deferred`, `assumes: [44,46,69,73]`) plus the 349-line design note `install-a-real-package.md` (commits 0b388b16, bd039b7d). Target: a single-rooted `src/`-layout package `memoria` (subpackages `operations/`, `mcp/`, `runtime/policy/`, `lib/`), `pyproject.toml` as single source of truth (hatchling, `dynamic` version, three dependency tiers replacing three `requirements*.txt`, `[project.scripts]` console entry points), deploy via a SHA256-pinned wheel into `<vault>/.memoria/.venv` so `.memoria/` holds *only* data + venv, never source. **Why:** the source tree and deploy location are the *same dotted directory* — `src/.memoria` is both authored code and rsync target — forcing three standing costs the ADR enumerates: a **dotted, un-importable** top-level name; **two parallel import mechanisms that must agree** (8 `sys.path` entries in `conftest.py` + 11 `Path(__file__)` bootstraps in the deployed runtime + a 12th in the policy plugin); and a delete-pruned two-phase rsync deploy. Research issue #494 asked the question; the ADR settles the target but **defers execution** because it changes both the deploy mechanism and on-disk vault shape (real blast radius) and must not churn the tree before the `engines→operations` rename lands. It explicitly corrects a "common misconception" — that ADR-55's golden copy protects runtime *code* — proving `golden.py`'s manifest has **no `.memoria/` prefix**, so code integrity is the MCP-only sandbox + Git, and ADR-55 is untouched. The one hard prerequisite it names is a security property, not a chore: the **policy-gate version-skew** decision (lean: gate calls the running policy MCP over the wire — structurally skew-free — rather than installing a second policy copy that could drift and wave through a mutating call). Linked to cadence-tracking issue #521 (mirrors ADR-63↔#413).

- **What:** The **actionable packaging slice** is scoped in the ExecPlan (Workstream E) to a **tooling-only `pyproject.toml`** — `[tool.pytest.ini_options]` (`pythonpath`) + `[tool.ruff]` only, deleting the `conftest.py` `sys.path` block, keeping `requirements-dev.txt`, adding no `[project]` table. **Why:** ADR-76's staged migration says step-1 is "issue work, no ADR" and safe to land anytime, while the deployment flip is gated on the skew decision and the rename; the ExecPlan's **guard** is "do not add a `[project]` table or change the deployment mechanism early — that drags target-stage risk forward with no benefit."

- **What:** ADR-76's `## When this matters` names distribution to non-checkout operators as a trigger, and records the wheel **strengthens** ADR-63 (multi-machine: build-once/install-on-N beats rsync-from-checkout) and is **in tension with** ADR-26 (the install unit shifts from rsynced subtree to a built wheel). **Why:** to keep the deferred decision honest at each cadence review rather than re-litigating it.

### UI / navigation / dashboards

- **What:** Turned the three Obsidian workspaces into named **intent gates** with new/rewritten dashboards: `desk.md` (new, "Action-first gate: what needs the PI now" — a "Needs me" inbox view, an "Act" button cluster for capture/delegate/resolve/Talk-to-Co-PI, and worker state), `library.md` (new, "Object-first gate: browse sources, Catalog records, and claims"), `studio.md` (new, "Synthesis gate: focus, claim corpus, pattern library"); wired into `home.md`, `workspaces.json`, and reference docs (commit 5c829df3). **Why:** implements ADR-70 (navigation — intent-named gates) which moved to `accepted` this release; the gates give each workspace a single job-to-be-done so "decision surfaces" (Desk) are separated from "literature objects" (Library) from "writing/synthesis" (Studio), with non-actionable health views pushed to left-sidebar tabs. Studio's header notes project-specific drafting "stays deferred" — the Project gate is not built (see design notes below).

- **What:** Made dashboard panes **action- and object-first** (#517, commit 129b6f79): `reading-pipeline.md` dropped its inline Dataview queries in favor of embedded `sources.base` / `claims.base` views ("Object-first Library view"), and `inbox.base` view ordering was changed to surface `action` and `finding` columns ahead of `type`/`certainty`/`lifecycle`. **Why:** the panes previously led with metadata; leading with the *action needed* and the *object in view* matches the intent-gate model (ADR-70) — the PI sees what to do / what to read before secondary attributes.

- **What:** Bundled the **Commander** community plugin (`cmdr` — data.json/main.js/manifest.json/styles.css) and registered it (commit 8680aed5). **Why:** implements ADR-72 (command surfacing — `accepted` this release): "every action reachable directly; Commander for placement, the Co-PI additive." Commander places the 16 QuickAdd command-palette macros onto toolbars/ribbons so PI direct-access does not depend on memorizing palette verbs.

- **What:** Bundled the **Modal Forms** plugin (30,832-line main.js + data.json/manifest/styles) and added a `docs/reference/vocabulary.md` reference page documenting the PI-editable controlled-value home (`system/vocabulary.md` feeding `research_area`, `methodology`, claim `topics`) (commit bc38948e). **Why:** implements ADR-71 (structured capture — forms at entry, the Linter as authority, one schema per type): surfacing the controlled vocabulary *through a form at capture time* keeps frontmatter values in lockstep with the vocabulary list rather than relying on free-text that later drifts and trips the Linter.

- **What:** Renamed command labels for consistency — `Memoria: delegate a task` → `delegate task`, `Memoria: workspace Desk/Library/Studio` → `open Desk/Library/Studio workspace`, and normalized `Talk to co-PI` → `Talk to Co-PI` across `home.md`, QuickAdd data, and ADR-68 prose (commits 8cc2afae, 20f2c506, 5c829df3). **Why:** command-and-skill-name alignment (#511/#508) — the palette verbs, QuickAdd scripts, and Commander placements must use one canonical string or the toolbar bindings and docs drift.

- **What:** Homepage startup now **replaces** the restored layout instead of stacking on it (#505, 1e5b2116). **Why:** listed in the ExecPlan as a defect fix; the front-door (ADR-13) must present a clean known state, not whatever Obsidian restored.

### Pipeline / ingest / capture

- **What:** Ingest now **creates a proposed source-note stub under `notes/source/` for the PI to fill** as part of the catalog-enrich flow — the `capture-from-url.js`, `capture-from-zotero.js`, `catalog-source.js` prompts and the `catalog-enrich-record` SKILL were updated to add "create the proposed source-note stub … then enrich … propose the classification" (#512, commit 612c0af8). **Why:** captures were landing a paper entity under `catalog/papers/` but no source note, so a captured item never appeared in the reading pipeline — the fix "surfaces url/zotero captures in inbox" (companion fixes #499, #507) so the object the PI reads is actually created at ingest, not left implicit.

- **What:** Zotero capture switched from **Better BibTeX CAYW to the BBT JSON-RPC endpoint** — `capture-from-zotero.js` now POSTs `item.citationkey(["selected"])` to `/better-bibtex/json-rpc` instead of GETting the CAYW URL, parsing citekeys from the RPC response (#525, commit f615115b). **Why:** listed as a fix ("use bbt json-rpc for zotero capture") — the CAYW format returned inconsistent citation-key fields (`citationKey`/`citekey`) and title data; the JSON-RPC `item.citationkey` call is the stable, purpose-built selection API. **Why not documented for the title drop:** inferred — the RPC returns citekeys only, so `title` is now set empty and resolved downstream during ingest.

- **What:** Added **create-linked-claim** (#513, commit c5010254): a new QuickAdd user script `create-linked-claim.js` that, from an active `notes/source/` note, creates a schema-shaped claim note (`type: claim`, `maturity: seedling`, `sources: [<citekey>]`), links it back into the source's frontmatter and under "Worth distilling," and opens it; a "Create linked claim" button was added to `templates/source.md`. **Why:** distillation (source → atomic claim) was a manual, error-prone hand-edit; scripting it enforces the frontmatter schema and the source↔claim link at creation, matching the PI direct-access rule (reachable from the source note itself).

- **What:** Linter detectors gained **findings telemetry** — `detectors.py` added `--jsonl-out` (append one JSON row per finding, create an empty file on clean runs) and `append_findings_jsonl()`; the lint cron wires it (#524, commit 4f384912). **Why:** listed as "emit lint findings telemetry" — Linter runs were report-only with no persisted trail, so trends (e.g. drift accumulation) couldn't be measured; a JSONL log makes findings a queryable metrics stream (feeds the status-line/dashboards work planned in the ExecPlan).

- **What:** Renamed `scripts/refresh-retraction-watch.sh` → `retraction-refresh-cron.sh` (and updated ADR-32's "Files affected") (commit 20f2c506 area). **Why:** naming clarity — the `-cron` suffix marks it as the scheduled refresh job for the retraction sweep engine (`engines/sweeps/retraction.py`), consistent with the other `*-cron.sh` wrappers.

### Gate / provenance / security

- **What:** ADR-32 **retired the Coder/Linter `terminal` exception** — annotated the Context note, Decision, and Least-privilege bullet to record that no profile ships `terminal`, `file`, or `code_execution`, enforced fail-closed by the policy plugin's denylist (commit 414efe65). **Why:** ADR-32's Decision still granted `terminal` to the Coder and Linter, **contradicting** ADR-48 (Linter became a no-agent engine), ADR-27 (Engineer is MCP-only), and the shipped implementation (all profile configs disable those toolsets; `policy_hook.py` hard-denies them). The prior Context note had fixed only the profile renames and even called the terminal stance "unchanged." This is a **zero-contradiction doc fix, not a decision reversal** — "the system already enforces this" — closing a residual doc-vs-implementation gap; only the external coding agent the Engineer delegates to runs outside the gate.

- **What:** Broadened `pr-policy` **sensitive paths** to include `AGENTS.md` and the agent-guidance directories (`.agents/`, `.claude/`, `.codex/`, `.kilo/`), routed `/security-review` at them, and narrowed `auto_approve` to prose paths (`docs/` except `docs/adr/`, or `_notes/`; `.md`/`.txt` only) (`AGENTS.md` diff, commit 012e376b area). **Why:** inferred from the Working-principles commit — agent guidance now *is* enforced policy (the new principles govern behavior), so edits to it carry the same review weight as `src/.memoria/` and `.github/`; letting it auto-approve would let agent policy change without human review.

- **What:** Made **cspell single-source** over all tracked markdown — moved the entire scope into `cspell.json` (`files: ["**/*.md"]` + `enableGlobDot` + `ignorePaths`) so CI and pre-commit both defer to it, renamed the required check to plain `cspell`, and added `tests/test_cspell_scope.py` to lock the invariant (commit 06d99620). **Why:** scope was defined in four drifting places (a cspell.yml git-ls-files grep, the pre-commit regex, and prose in two docs) and "one copy had already diverged" — a live instance of the zero-contradiction failure the release is systematically hunting. Broadened coverage to 390 files (adds `.agents/`, tests README, PR template) with 0 issues.

### Profiles / runtime / skills

- **What:** Renamed three Co-PI skills to match their command names — `explain-the-system` → `explain-system`, `explore-branch-framings` → `explore-framings`, `delegate-route-task` → `route-task` — and aligned the `ask-question-source` / `ask-read-lens` skill references and `memoria-copi/SOUL.md` (#511, commit 8cc2afae). **Why:** command↔skill name drift meant a palette verb and the skill it invokes had different slugs, an alignment defect the release is closing across the surface.

- **What:** Normalized **`co-PI` → `Co-PI`** casing fleet-wide — across ADR-46 (including its title), ADR-48 (title), ADR-3/26/55/63/68, the ADR README index, SOUL.md, home.md, and profile config (commits 20f2c506, and the ADR sweep). **Why:** "align Co-PI casing and agent-client exports" (#508) — a single canonical capitalization for the permanent conversational agent, another zero-contradiction hygiene pass.

- **What:** Kept the fleeting template **YAML plain** (#504, commit 270ff6d0) and fixed inbox-resolve lifecycle validity (#500) and delegate-task picker labels (#501). **Why:** listed as defect fixes in the ExecPlan defect workstream; templated frontmatter that isn't plain YAML breaks Bases/Dataview parsing.

### ADRs (decisions governing the above)

- **What:** New **ADR-75** — "Use GitHub Project fields and release sub-issues for live work state" (`accepted`, `assumes: [45]`) (commit sequence around 5c829df3/012e376b). **Why:** ADR-45 had moved release readiness into a single "Release vX.Y" *checklist* issue, but that made each gate a checkbox rather than a work item with its own owner, evidence, and blocking discussion, and labels had accreted five meanings (type/area/priority/triage/bot). Decision: the **Memoria Issue Tracker** Project carries `Status`/`Area`/`Type`/`Priority` fields, labels stay minimal, and readiness becomes a **parent "Release vX.Y" issue with one sub-issue per gate/stage**. Rejected alternatives (recorded): keep the flat checklist (no per-gate evidence trail), use labels for the field schema (labels are search chips + bot hooks, not a planning schema), track state in markdown (reintroduces the drift class ADR-45 removed). This drove the parallel rewrites of `AGENTS.md` work-routing, `docs/releasing/README.md`, and the release-plan template (folder-per-version + thin README + `tmp/`; readiness in sub-issues; internal checkpoints use `status: complete`/`released: false`).

- **What:** Promoted **ADR-69, 70, 71, 72, 73** from `proposed` → `accepted` (dropping `nav_exclude`), dated 2026-06-14 (ADR README + individual diffs). **Why:** these are the alpha.3/alpha.4 design decisions (operations-layer naming; intent-named navigation gates; structured capture forms; command surfacing; docs-reference conventions) that the shipped UI/vocabulary/Commander work in this release implements — accepting them settles the vocabulary the code now builds on (ADR-69's own note: "the vocabulary decision is wanted now so UI work builds on settled terms"; the tree rename stays a separately-sequenced pass).

- **What:** ADR-73 promoted its `check_site_local_links` docs-doctor check from **advisory → blocking** ("`docs-doctor` blocks published→`src/` relative links"). **Why:** the published-site link hygiene sweep it was staging is complete, so the guard is now enforced rather than warn-only.

- **What:** Folded #194's borrowable ideas into existing deferred-integration registers rather than opening new issues — **ADR-58** names **Quartz** as the candidate static-HTML report renderer (and downstream renderer for the open-design deliverable flow), and **ADR-61** adds a packaged cross-lane **"deep research" macro** (after Khoj's scheduled-automation mode) built on the nightly discovery loop (commit cd74e03a, closes #194). **Why:** the comparative-repos survey surfaced two ideas that "belong in the existing deferred-integration registers rather than as new issues" — keeping them as ADR extension-notes prevents backlog bloat while preserving the provenance (the #194 survey) and the boundary discipline (an extension of the same loop, "not a separate runtime / competing system").

- **What:** Re-framed the retired-Project-workflow references across **ADR-3, 21, 47** — "the v0.1.0-alpha.3 Project release" → "the deferred Project workflow" (and ADR-26/45/46/48/55/63 path/casing touch-ups: `docs/releasing/vX.Y/` → `<version>/`, etc.). **Why:** the Project gate slipped its target (ADR-70 deferred it; `projects/` still ships empty), so ADRs that promised it "returns in alpha.3" were stale — the zero-contradiction sweep repoints them to a version-neutral "deferred Project workflow."

### Design notes authored here, then deferred to alpha.5

- **What:** Authored `test-env.md` — a **clean-sheet, all-Linux test harness** design (281 lines) — then moved it forward to `docs/releasing/0.1.0-alpha.5/tmp/` as a git rename (commits 0145dc3f then 7dd0d09f). It proposes **two single-OS installers** replacing the old split-OS bridge: `install.ps1` (all-Windows = production, native Hermes per ADR-64, localhost only) and `install.sh` (all-Linux = test, containerized/ephemeral, GPU-served local model, fully automatable). The Linux env is a version-controlled golden-image Docker Compose stack (native Hermes + 5 profiles + headless Obsidian via `xvfb-run` + Local REST/MCP + Zotero + qmd + fixture vault) driven by a pytest orchestrator over the 16 command-palette commands, with a local **Gemma 4 12B (GGUF Q4_K_M) served by llama.cpp** (`--jinja`), full L0–L5 coverage plus new chaos/security/performance suites. **Why:** the prior shipped posture — Obsidian-on-Windows ↔ Hermes-in-WSL2 bridged over mirrored-networking loopback — existed "only because we lacked native-Windows Hermes and a Linux GUI stack"; now that both exist, the note deletes the bridge and its whole "topology parity" fragility class rather than working around it. It's ADR-owned (supersedes/amends ADR-29 L3, ADR-31 transport, revisits ADR-64) and explicitly flags a **process risk**: it supersedes a recorded memory decision but the superseding ADR "does not exist yet" — write the ADR before cleanup. **Why moved:** the ExecPlan judged it "not alpha.4 work" and pushed it to alpha.5 planning (#530).

- **What:** Authored `project-starter.md` — the **Project gate** design (the fourth navigation gate deferred by ADR-70, the empty `projects/` from ADR-68; 678 lines) — then moved it to alpha.5/tmp (commits 0145dc3f, 7dd0d09f). Core model: **two graphs, not one** — a bottom-up descriptive knowledge map (Zettelkasten/MOC tradition) *and* a top-down Toulmin argument graph (`supports`/`contradicts`/`warrant` rooted at a thesis), where the **outline derives from the argument graph, not the topology** ("that single distinction is what moves the gate from 'organizes knowledge' to 'produces an argument'"); thesis-as-provisional-claim as the anchor; structural impact/saturation/termination as deterministic **Operations** in the same trust class as the contradictions dashboard. **Why:** keeps the gate inside the architecture's deepest invariant (agents propose, PI promotes, nothing auto-infers — ADR-10/48/51) — its *logic* is bias-free and replayable, never asking an LLM to judge. It states the **two-tier determinism rule** as its load-bearing honesty guard: a structural Operation can check that a thing is *articulated* (tier 2 — cheap, auditable, **gameable**) but not that it is *good* (tier 3 — PI or gated agent judgment); "determinism buys auditability of the computation, not correctness of the conclusion." **Why moved:** not alpha.4 work (#530); the Project gate build stays deferred, so Studio's dashboard still notes project drafting is out of scope.

---

### Removed / retired

- **What:** Deleted the alpha.3 `tmp/` design-scratch (7 files: `alpha3-triage`, `design-notes-1`, `issue-tracking-guide`, `naming-and-diataxis-audit`, `open-issues-research`, `project-field-mapping`, `ui-design-research-report`) and the completed alpha.3 issue guide (commits 290eecaf, dc51f992, 726f6b86). **Why:** by the new routing rule (`AGENTS.md`, releasing README, ExecPlan playbook), `tmp/` release-scratch is a working artifact **deleted before the release/checkpoint closes** — durable outputs already routed to ADRs/issues, so keeping the scratch would violate the "no fourth permanent record" principle.

- **What:** Retired the **Coder/Linter `terminal` capability** in doc form (ADR-32, ADR-21's autonomy exception already retired) — see Gate section. **Why:** doc caught up to an already-enforced implementation; no runtime behavior changed.

- **What:** Retired the CAYW Zotero read path (replaced by JSON-RPC) and the four-place cspell scope definition (collapsed into `cspell.json`). **Why:** both were drift/fragility sources replaced by a single canonical mechanism (see Pipeline and Security sections).

*Note on scope: the `engines→operations` rename (ADR-69), ingest source tiers (#438/#437 Unpaywall/PubMed), golden-copy upgrade reconcile (#339, ADR-55), Mapper Tier 2 (#439, ADR-19), and native Windows `install.ps1` (#414/#296, ADR-64) are **planned and scoped in the alpha.4 ExecPlan** but their implementation PRs land after `b1657d92` — they are not code changes in this range.*

## alpha.5 — The Project gate (the fourth navigation gate becomes real)

alpha.5 fills ADR-70's deferred fourth-gate slot and ADR-68's empty `projects/` folder with a working **Project gate**: a bounded research inquiry that drives an argument toward a *defended or falsified* thesis and — the headline job — **knows when to stop** (saturation), inverting the treadmill where a dashboard's implicit purpose is to keep generating work. The release was driven by one converged design note (`project-starter.md`) whose central bet is that the gate's *logic* must be a deterministic Operation in the same trust class as the contradictions/knowledge-map views (auditable, replayable, bias-free) while its *inputs* stay PI-authored or agent-proposed-then-gated — never an LLM judging truth. It ships the deliberately narrowed **expanded v1 cut** (everything deterministic or free), pairs the gate with a coordinated ADR housekeeping sweep (three new ADRs, one recast, two rejections, one supersession), and clears cheap unblocked backlog slices (graded-loudness block gate, attention instrumentation, hub-handoff tier 2, PubMed/OA ingest, a visual design system). The WS-0 spikes de-risked the two structural forks up front (the Bases custom-view API and the maturity threshold), so the data model was never gated on rendering tech.

---

### Vault / concepts

**What:** Two net-new note types — `project` and `thesis` — added under `src/.memoria/schemas/types/{project,thesis}.yaml` + `src/system/templates/{project,thesis}.md`, both `category: projects`, `gated: false`. `project` carries `slug`, `scope_topics`, `inquiry` (PICO map), `finer` map, `output_mode: thesis|survey`, `question_version`, `question_log`, and `active_thesis`; lifecycle is only `[current, archived]`. `thesis` carries the full chain `proposed → provisional → current → retracted → archived` with `promotion_gate: current` and `initial_lifecycle: proposed`. — **Why:** the design's schema-grounded correction (§4): a `claim` cannot host a provisional position because `claim.yaml`'s lifecycle is `[current, retracted, archived]` — claims are *born canonical* (ADR-49/50), so "a provisional claim" is a schema contradiction. Forcing a thesis canonical "manufactures the premature-thesis / sunk-cost artifact this design exists to avoid" (ADR-78 Context; `project-starter.md` §4). The question and thesis are split into two artifacts because they are "different parts of speech" — interrogative+scoped vs. declarative — so a changed question triggers a staleness cascade while a changed thesis is ordinary hypothesis revision (ADR-78 Alternatives).

**What:** Project *status* is not stored — it is derived from the active thesis's lifecycle and `output_mode` (there is no project status field). — **Why:** follows ADR-10's precedent of "deriving state from structure rather than adding a parallel status field"; one lifecycle field absorbs output-mode visibility, project status, falsification-as-result, and mode transition (`project-starter.md` §4). A `retracted` thesis plus the subgraph that refuted it is a *finished* project, not a dead end (ADR-77/78 Consequences).

**What:** Folder renames `notes/source → notes/sources` and `notes/index → notes/indexes` (`schemas/folders.yaml` `homes` + `skeleton`; `.gitkeep` moves; all skill `write_scope`/descriptions, link-color CSS, and map skills updated). New homes `project: projects`, `thesis: projects`, `worklist-item: system/worklists`; new skeleton dirs `projects/_template/{code,drafts,exports}` and `system/worklists`. — **Why:** the project scaffold needs a per-project workspace shape (`projects/<slug>/` with code/drafts/exports), created by `start-project.js` (ADR-77 Consequences). The `source`/`index` pluralization is a consistency cleanup carried alongside the new folders; inferred housekeeping, not separately documented.

**What:** `worklist-item` note type added (`system/worklists/`, `worklists.base` with By-worklist/By-decision/By-group views) — `decision: [proposed, include, exclude, maybe, archived]`, `worklist`, `item_ref`, `rank`, `group`. — **Why:** materializes ADR-54's batch-worklist surface (folds #555 "batch worklist surface"); the ADR-audit found ADR-54 shipped only as a fleeting note + aggregate card, not the per-row Bases surface the prose promised (`adr-update.md` §1.2) — this closes that gap: one aggregate work-prompt per batch, each row a `worklist-item` note.

**What:** Schema field additions on existing types: `claim.yaml` and `thesis.yaml` `links` gain an optional `warrant` on `supports` entries (comment-level, not enforced); `paper.yaml` gains `ingest_status: [tier0, enriched, complete, needs-human]`; `source.yaml` gains `evidence_level: [cebm-1…cebm-5, ungraded]`; `gap.yaml` gains `gap_type: [additive, conflict, fragility, structural, unstated-warrant, refutation]` plus derived-cache fields (`impact`, `on_path`, `saturation_state`, `graph_maturity`, `computed_at`). — **Why:** `warrant` is reserved as an *optional attribute only* (Toulmin's "frequently left unstated" inferential rule) but deliberately NOT mandated — §13.2/ADR-79 rule it "the single biggest labor sink in the design for the least deterministic payoff," gameable as a tier-2 presence check, so v1 reserves the shape and leaves the unstated-warrant gap detector off. `ingest_status` fixes the ADR-30 audit finding that the field was "written by engine code but not declared in `paper.yaml`, so it escapes schema validation" (`adr-update.md` §1.2). `evidence_level` (CEBM) is "the one genuinely mechanical bridge between reliability and impact" — a rankable enum that can feed impact triage (`project-starter.md` §11). `gap_type` generalizes the ADR-51 `gap` card beyond "missing-source need" to the full missing-vs-contested taxonomy (§6, §16).

---

### Gate / provenance / the deterministic engine

**What:** New Operation `src/.memoria/operations/processing/project/structural_impact.py` (~800 lines) — the whole gate spine. It reads the thesis-rooted `supports`/`contradicts` subgraph, computes the connected component, articulation points (Tarjan DFS), and per-note **impact** via lost-reachability-from-thesis (falling back to degree for non-articulation nodes), and writes ONE generated `projects/<slug>/project-gate-index.md` with `computed_at`/`stale` and per-note derived values, embedding a machine-readable JSON block between HTML comment markers. — **Why:** Bases "reads only frontmatter, never note bodies, and cannot traverse graphs" (§12), so impact/saturation/maturity *cannot* be Bases formulas — they need a deterministic traversal Operation. Materializing to a **single index-note** rather than per-note stamps is the WS-0 §13.4 verdict: because the `registerBasesView` API was verified usable (§D3), pay the custom-view cost once and honor the "write notes once" discipline / avoid the ADR-25 append-only audit write-amplification a per-component re-stamp would cause (`ws-0-spikes.md`; `project-starter.md` §12/§D4). The index-note also self-excludes from the scan (`generated_by: memoria-structural-impact`).

**What:** The **maturity threshold** is hard-coded conservative: a thesis component is `mature` only when connected with `>= 5` addressed relations including `>= 1 supports` AND `>= 1 contradicts` (`MATURITY_RELATION_THRESHOLD = 5`); below that it is `immature`/`cold-start` and the payload returns `displayed_confidence: below-threshold`. — **Why:** §13.1, resolved in WS-0 and recorded in ADR-77: this is "the gate's trust switch… the parameter the gate's safety rests on, not a knob to tune after launch." Set too low and the gate "asserts confidence on a sparse graph — the automation-bias failure the whole design exists to prevent"; too high and it never terminates. "Lowering this threshold is a safety change, not a preference" (`project-starter.md` §13.1; `ws-0-spikes.md` §13.1). The `>=1 contradicts` requirement encodes Popper: a thesis corroborated only by accumulated `supports` "looks complete but is intellectually untested" (§5).

**What:** **Saturation** gates on three conditions in code: (1) `maturity == mature`; (2) `high_open_gaps == 0` (no on-path gap with impact `>= HIGH_IMPACT_THRESHOLD = 2`); (3) a structural refutation floor (a `contradicts` edge touching the thesis) AND a PI-set `refutation_sufficiency` truthy stamp on the project/thesis. `cold-start` forces `saturation_state: unknown`. — **Why:** this is *theoretical* saturation / Dey's "theoretical sufficiency," not data saturation (§5). Naïve "all gaps below threshold" is "true on an empty project" (fires at birth) and "true on an unchallenged thesis." Conditions 1–2 are "fully structural… replaces an unprovable prediction with a checkable fact about topology"; condition 3 is the irreducible tier-3 judgment that "resists structural formulation," so v1 collapses it to a **one-click PI-asserted `refutation_sufficiency` stamp** rather than a standing honesty-card nag (§5, §19). Honest caveat recorded: the stamp is itself gameable — "an acceptable 'trust the solo PI' choice for v1."

**What:** **Gap taxonomy** in code: three confident, zero-authoring kinds ship (`additive`, `conflict`, `fragility` — `CONFIDENT_GAP_KINDS`); `structural`/`refutation` are computed but emitted as `ADVISORY_GAP_KINDS`; `unstated-warrant` is absent. — **Why:** §13.5 chose "three, not two and not six," discriminated by *authoring cost*: fragility is "free — a degree query, zero PI authoring" so the reviewers' proposed strip-to-two "drops this for nothing." Structural is deterministic-but-niche, refutation folds into saturation condition 3 as a stamp, and unstated-warrant needs the not-shipped `warrant` (§13.5 table). Advisory items are "collapsed, uncounted, on-demand, and *hidden* (not greyed) below the maturity threshold — so the dashboard never becomes a guilt ledger" (§19).

**What:** **Cold-start** two-regime triage: below maturity the Operation uses `scope_overlap` (project `scope_topics` ∩ note terms) rather than argument-structure impact. — **Why:** §8 — impact ranking "is weakest precisely when orientation is most needed," so the honest fix is to name the regime: scope-overlap is deterministic (via ADR-15 `project-hints` topics) and "never forces a tier-3 jump," and the dashboard displays low confidence instead of a confident-looking meaningless ranking.

**What:** **Graded-loudness block gate** — new `operations/lib/loudness.py` + `policy_mcp.py` now denies any mutating action to a review-gated path when open `loudness: block` + `lifecycle: proposed` inbox cards exist (`policy_rule: loudness.block.active`), returning the blockers; `alert`/`block` cards are pushed to Telegram (best-effort, logged to `loudness-push.jsonl`), `quiet`/`notice` stay pull-only. — **Why:** commit #549/#610 — loudness stops being pure display metadata and gains routing semantics: "open block cards pause delegation and review-gated promotion until the PI acknowledges them." This is the safety-valve that lets a structural invalidation (thesis supersession, question-revision cascade) reserve the loud channel — §12's rule that "staleness ≠ urgency; reserve the loud channel for invalidation."

**What:** Audit log entries now stamp `schema_version: 2` and `review_mode: blocking` on every append (`policy_mcp.py append_audit`). — **Why:** the ADR-audit's ADR-41 "stamping sliver" — "stamp `review_mode: blocking` + bump `schema_version` now (attribution is non-backfillable); advisory behavior stays deferred" (`adr-update.md` §2.3/§4.2). Provenance attribution can't be added retroactively, so the cheap stamp lands even while the advisory feature waits.

**What:** New `cron_heartbeat.py` writes `system/logs/cron-heartbeat.jsonl` (last-successful-run per job); cron wrappers (`*-cron.sh`) updated to call it. — **Why:** the "start-now instrumentation" principle (`adr-update.md` §3.3): deferred always-on triggers (ADR-63) "can never self-detect" without the log — the heartbeat lets a future "recorded cron miss with sleep already disabled" trigger fire from data rather than PI memory.

---

### ADRs (decisions that governed the release)

**What:** Three new ADRs accepted 2026-06-16 — **ADR-77 Project gate** (`assumes: [68,70,48,49,51,69]`), **ADR-78 Thesis note type** (`assumes: [50,77]`), **ADR-79 Argument graph and warrant** (`assumes: [8,52,77,78]`). — **Why:** the `project-starter.md` §18 build plan called for exactly three ADRs (project gate umbrella; thesis-as-distinct-type resolving the claim-born-current conflict; argument-graph+warrant as a separate testable decision extending ADR-52's deliberate minimalism). ADR-77 records the conservative maturity default and index-note materialization as durable decisions; ADR-79 reserves `warrant` optional and keeps the unstated-warrant detector off "until relation coverage and PI demand justify it."

**What:** **ADR-76 fully recast**: `76-runtime-as-installable-package.md` → `76-versioned-vault-release-reconciling-installer.md`, title "Package the Python runtime as an installable wheel; vault holds data, not source" → "Distribute Memoria as a versioned vault release; deploy via a source-agnostic reconciling installer" (`assumes` gains `55`; still `deferred`). — **Why:** the clean-slate redesign in `install-a-real-package.md` found the wheel framing "optimizes only the first of three" deployment layers and is "wrong as the deployment spine": a wheel cannot carry `SOUL.md`/`SKILL.md`, the host-loaded `plugin.yaml` gate shim, or cron wrappers, so "vault holds data, not source" is *unreachable*. The inverted spine: the unit is a versioned vault release; `install(release_root, vault_path)` is a pure reconciling function over three lifecycle layers (code→venv, authored-content→three-way-merge, per-vault-state→untouched); one content-addressable manifest does triple duty (golden drift, gate version assertion, tamper verification); a tiny standalone **policy core** dissolves gate-vs-runtime version skew *structurally* rather than parking it as an execution blocker. The `engines → operations` rename that had *sequenced before* packaging having landed (#536) freed the recast. Editable install (`pip install -e .`) is the principled default to keep deployed code inspectable; no wheel is shipped.

**What:** **ADR-34 (Code-artifact autopilot) and ADR-40 (Admin/forensic GUI) → rejected**; **ADR-17 (Shared candidate frontmatter) → superseded by [50,51]** — all `date_resolved: 2026-06-16`. Ripple edits: ADR-61 `assumes` drops 34 and re-points 37→48; ADR-58 `assumes` drops 40; ADR-50/51 gain `supersedes: [17]`. — **Why:** the 2026-06-15 ADR audit (`adr-update.md` §5). ADR-34 is "structurally precluded by ADR-21 (L3 ceiling)… declined, not parked." ADR-40's forensic need "is met by the CLI + dashboards now and the (deferred) ADR-58 read-only Inspector later; an external admin GUI would add a second un-gated write surface — declined on architecture, not tool maturity." ADR-17 was "silently superseded" — the shipped `type: candidate` uses ADR-50/51's honesty-card fields, and ADR-17's normative schema (`candidate-note`, `candidate_status`, folder `99-system/`) "does not exist."

**What:** **ADR-19 tier-2 ships** — retitled "Agent-proposed MOCs" → "Agent-proposed hubs (threshold alert and Mapper handoff)"; new `operations/integrity/linter/hub_handoff.py` reads fired `hub-threshold` findings and raises an idempotent `map`-lane card; ceiling-validated by `tasks_mcp.py`, allowed writes only `notes/fleeting/maps/` + `inbox/`, `notes/hubs/` explicitly forbidden. — **Why:** #557 "hub threshold mapper handoff." Tier 1 (report-only) had shipped; the asymmetry was that a `reference-note` gets agent help while a `hub` was "human-authored start to finish" even though the Mapper "already computes the exact signal a hub proposal needs." The mitigation is enforced structurally: the stub is "a member list + threshold note only, never annotations — because the annotation *is* the curation that defines the type, and that is the human's" (ADR-19 Trade-offs).

**What:** A coordinated doc-integrity pass across ~30 ADRs (status/trigger/citation fixes from the audit): ADR-62 aggregator marked built; ADR-44 "zero test code" reconciled; ADR-30 `ingest_status` enum; ADR-65 `assumes` corrected to drop `8` (keep `52,30`); ADR-61 `assumes` 37→48 and ADR-37/ADR-17 references re-pointed; ADR-18 alias note; ADR-54 worklist clarification; ADR-69 engines→operations recorded as fully executed. — **Why:** the audit ran a 7-agent parallel pass over 76 ADRs then a red-team pass that caught several *stale* reads before they were executed (`adr-update.md` §6) — e.g. "ADR-59 scorer does NOT ship" (the decouple stands but is build-then-shadow), "ADR-65 `assumes` is `[8,52,30]` not `[8]`" (dropping `8` not "[8]→[52]", which would have lost the `30` ingest dep), "the `find-duplicates` sweep does not exist — build-first," NeMo-SemDedup ≠ 0.8, PRISMA-2020 is a reporting guideline (Cochrane Rapid Reviews is the single-screen source, MECIR C40 mandates dual). The corrections were applied inline "so the eventual `docs/adr/` PR is clean and `gen_adr_index.py` passes."

---

### Profiles / runtime

**What:** `engines/ → operations/` layer rename executed across the tree (ADR-69): `operations/{lib,integrity,processing,telemetry,cleanup}/…`; every reference updated (profile `config.yaml` retraction path, `board_export.py` `_LIB_DIR`, `policy_mcp.py` design comment, `calibration.yaml` archive-sweep path, skills). — **Why:** ADR-69 operations-layer naming, landed via #536/#541/#542 — the audit confirmed it "now fully executed" and a prerequisite that had been sequenced *before* the ADR-76 packaging spine, freeing that recast (`adr-update.md` §1.4/§6).

**What:** Obsidian MCP transport hardened from plain-HTTP loopback to **HTTPS with certificate verification** in the Writer/Peer-reviewer/Librarian `config.yaml`: `url: https://127.0.0.1:${OBSIDIAN_MCP_PORT}/mcp` + `ssl_verify: ${OBSIDIAN_MCP_SSL_VERIFY}` pointing at the plugin's exported PEM cert/CA bundle. — **Why:** the prior comment admitted "Hermes can't skip TLS verify for the self-signed HTTPS port, hence plain HTTP on loopback" — a security compromise. Native Windows install support (#570) surfaced the exported-cert path that lets Hermes verify TLS properly, closing the plaintext-loopback gap. Inferred from the config comment rewrite; tied to the alpha.4-native-Windows install reconciliation.

---

### Pipeline / ingest / enrichment

**What:** New OA extraction sources in `operations/processing/ingest/extract.py` — Unpaywall (DOI → best OA PDF → `pymupdf4llm`) as first-lookup tier, and PMC full-text; PDF parsing runs in a resource-limited (`RLIMIT_CPU`/`RLIMIT_AS`) subprocess. — **Why:** #537 "add PubMed and OA extraction sources." "OA copy may have a better text layer than a scanned attachment, so the tiers are" ordered Unpaywall-first (extract.py docstring). The resource-limited subprocess enforces ADR-30's deterministic-ingest safety (a malformed/hostile PDF cannot exhaust the host).

**What:** Ingest operations (`classify.py`, `link.py`, `ingest_paper.py`, `resolve_merge.py`, `runner.py`) relocated under `operations/processing/ingest/`; `ingest_status` now schema-validated. — **Why:** the operations rename (above) plus the ADR-30 schema-validation fix.

---

### Retrieval / derived store

**What:** The **materialized derived-property cache** is introduced as first-class infrastructure: one generated `project-gate-index.md` per project holding `impact`/`on_path`/`saturation_state`/`graph_maturity`/`computed_at`, written *only when values change*, read by a custom `registerBasesView`. — **Why:** §12 corrected an earlier overclaim — "Nothing in Memoria today writes derived properties back onto existing-note frontmatter… this must be owned as a first-class design decision," with two rules: **write-only-on-change** (against ADR-25 append-only write amplification) and **`computed_at` + visible staleness** ("Bases has no auto-refresh… the persisted values are a materialized cache with a real write cost — not free, not silently current"). WS-0 verified `registerBasesView` in `obsidian@1.13.1`, so the index-note path (not per-note stamps) was chosen.

---

### UI / navigation / dashboards

**What:** `home.md` status line rewritten from the "Status glance" info callout to a `[!brief]` status line reading verdict + Active/Waiting/Review/Retries/Alerts/Blocks from `board-state.jsonl` totals, lint verdicts, and open alert/block inbox cards; dashboard section callouts changed `[!example]` → `[!suggestions]`. — **Why:** #546 "ship home status line" + #547 "callout producers" + #556 "enforce visual design system" — the home page becomes a live single-glance operational readout surfacing the new retrying queue-depth and the graded-loudness alert/block counts (the same signals the block gate acts on).

**What:** New `project-gate.base` + `project-gate.md` dashboard (Active-projects grouped by output_mode; a "Needs refutation stamp" view filtering `output_mode == thesis AND refutation_sufficiency != true`); `worklists.base`; `fleet-health.md` de-placeholdered with a live Dataview table (trust score, gate/expand/open-resolve minutes, blind samples, cost). — **Why:** ADR-77 makes Project "a first-class navigation destination rather than a promise hidden behind Studio." The "Needs refutation stamp" view operationalizes saturation condition 3 as a visible PI to-do. Fleet-health losing its `[placeholder]` marker reflects the ADR-62 audit finding that the aggregator "is built and cron-wired" (`adr-update.md` §1.1).

**What:** Four new QuickAdd PI scripts: `start-project.js` (Modal Forms `memoria-project-start` → scaffolds `projects/<slug>/` with project+thesis notes and code/drafts/exports); `supersede-thesis.js` (mark-don't-invalidate pivot — new proposed thesis, `superseded_by` on the old, updates `active_thesis`, raises an alert card for lazy re-confirmation); `refresh-project-gate.js` (runs `structural_impact.py` against the active project, resolving the venv python cross-platform); `verify-draft.js` extended to detect ungrounded assertions and emit knowledge-gap cards. — **Why:** G4 ("a PI can drive a project end-to-end from Obsidian"). Supersession implements §15's central correction: an earlier draft said edges "do not auto-carry — re-confirm each by hand," which "reimposed the exact sunk-cost trap §4 exists to remove"; the fix is "carry the former edges forward as `stale`, re-confirm only the on-path/high-impact ones, lazily" so "a just-pivoted thesis is not done, but the pivot is *cheap*." verify-draft realizes §6's "writing is a gap-generator, not a terminal sink" — "the draft is the best gap-detector… every assertion not grounded in a `current` claim emits a knowledge-gap."

**What:** New Obsidian `assist.js` verb surface (Find/Search/Ask/Draft/Explore/Patterns from the palette, selection-aware, results forced to staging) and `structured-source-capture.js` form. — **Why:** #551 "Obsidian assist surface" (#380 verb-shaped PI entry) and #554 "structured source capture form" — a staged-proposal complement to the conversational Agent Client pane, hard-wired so "results must land as proposals in staging… do not write directly to canonical/current notes," preserving the propose-don't-promote invariant.

**What:** Visual design system enforced — new `memoria-property-badges.css` (lifecycle/loudness state accents with a `@settings` block), `memoria-link-colors.css` gains lifecycle accents (proposed/provisional/current/retracted/archived), both enabled by default in `appearance.json`. — **Why:** #556 "enforce visual design system" (#145) — "color the states that decide what needs attention," making proposed/needs-PI and block/retracted states visually salient, consistent with the block-gate and status-line signals.

---

### Distribution / evaluation / measurement

**What:** **Attention (PI-touch) instrumentation** added to `metrics_aggregate.py` — reads `system/logs/attention.jsonl` (Obsidian-side resolve timing: `card_open_resolve_min`, `expand_then_accept_min`) and per-lane board timings (`time_on_gate_min`), plus trigger-telemetry logs (#609); surfaced in fleet-health. — **Why:** G5 "instrument-as-gate, the safety valve for the expanded cut," implementing §14's PI-labor budget: "inference-free is PI-labor-full." "Measure it… track per-project PI touch count… If a project costs hundreds of clicks before it terminates, the leverage the gate promises has evaporated" (§14). The v1 cut mandates "commit a PI-touch budget before launch… gap-kind and warrant expansion unlock only after one real project comes in under budget" (§19).

**What:** **Blind re-review sampling** — `board_export.py` deterministically SHA-samples ~5% of terminal reviews (or forced via `blind_rereview: true`) into `blind-review-samples.jsonl`; aggregated per-lane in metrics. — **Why:** #608 "instrument review gate attention metrics" — a deterministic second-pass sampler measuring the review gate's own reliability without a mutable sampler state (the card id hash "makes the same choice without a mutable sampler state"). Ties to the ADR-16 audit note on "AI-as-second-screener with κ computed deterministically."

**What:** Native Windows install support and installer golden-copy reconciliation on upgrades (#570, #538); setup guides aligned; Obsidian MCP port added to installer inputs (#571). — **Why:** ADR-76's step-2 packaging half "stands on its own import-hygiene merits" and the reconciling installer must "three-way reconcile" authored content "so customizations surface, not clobber" — the golden-copy-on-upgrade reconciliation is that mechanism landing early, and native Windows unblocked the HTTPS-cert MCP path.

---

### Security

**What:** The MCP-only sandbox gains an active *block* dimension (loudness block gate above) and the audit trail gains `schema_version`/`review_mode` stamps; the deny path is asserted by test (#610 "policy gate deny assertion"). — **Why:** §12's corrected gating analysis: `policy_hook` gates agent/Hermes writes but a *human* base-board drag "writes through Obsidian directly, and ADR-49's Linter monitor catches it only post-hoc." The real risk is "ritual erosion — a one-gesture drag canonizes without the honesty-card review the gate exists to force," so "a gated transition must route through the review step, never a column drag" — which is exactly why the thesis lifecycle is deliberately NOT a draggable Kanban and the block gate denies mutating writes to gated zones while a block card is open.

**What:** Obsidian MCP TLS verification (covered under Profiles/runtime) closes the plaintext-loopback compromise. — **Why:** as above; the prior HTTP-on-loopback was an explicit acknowledged workaround now removed.

---

### Removed / retired (and why)

- **ADR-34 (Code-artifact autopilot) — rejected.** Structurally precluded by ADR-21's L3 autonomy ceiling; any code-lane execution is the separate #369 "define the code lane" decision, "not an autopilot" (`adr-update.md` §5). Coding is also explicitly out of scope for the Project gate (§10 — "code output has a different artifact lattice… and a different lane").
- **ADR-40 (Admin/forensic GUI) — rejected.** Forensic need met by CLI + dashboards now and the deferred ADR-58 read-only Inspector later; a GUI "would add a second un-gated write surface — declined on architecture, not tool maturity" (§5).
- **ADR-17 (Shared candidate frontmatter) — superseded by [50,51].** The normative schema never shipped; the live `type: candidate` is ADR-51's honesty card. The stale `candidate-note`/`candidate_status`/`99-system/` schema body was dropped (§5).
- **The shipped-wheel deployment spine (old ADR-76) — discarded.** Kept only as its "code-layer install mechanism"; dropped as the *shipped artifact* because it can't carry the authored two-thirds, adds a premature supply-chain trust surface + non-atomic `pip --upgrade` rollback, and left gate skew "an open execution blocker" (new ADR-76 Alternatives).
- **Explicitly deferred, each for a named reason (release-plan §5):** the full ephemeral test-env harness (ADR-77/78 of that effort — alpha.5 ships only the thin S5 validation slice); the **inference tier** (tier-3 semantic impact / any LLM judging the gate — "breaks the auditability the gate rests on"); a `warrant` *mandate* and the unstated-warrant gap; multi-thesis projects and auto-promotion of gated transitions; **ADR-61's nightly autonomous loop** — *not accepted to unblock the gate* because gap-pull already works as on-demand `find` via the unified Librarian (ADR-48, per ADR-37's supersession note), and ADR-61's own adoption conditions (always-on deploy, maintained `research-focus.md`, a written screening-plan) are unmet, its `assumes` stale (§11/§13.3).

## alpha.6 — Conformance closeout & the model-free test-env harness (ADR-80 Phase 1)

**Theme:** make the *accepted* decisions that silently didn't hold actually hold, then ship the roadmap's committed-next automated verification spine.

alpha.6 is an internal, untagged checkpoint (`status: complete`, `released: false`) built on two pillars. Pillar one (Track A) turns the findings of a full accepted-ADR audit — all 56 accepted ADRs read against the *built* artifacts, which found 8 partials and 0 unbuilt (`docs/releasing/0.1.0-alpha.6/tmp/adr-implementation-gap-analysis.md`) — into real conformance fixes: a runtime-security regression, two unenforced schema/query invariants, the missing Project-gate navigation surface, and cheap docs/template/supply-chain cleanups. Pillar two (Track B) delivers the long-pole net-new work: the **ephemeral test-env harness (ADR-80, Phase 1)**, a model-free L0–L4 golden path via seed→cassette that makes every future release re-runnable from a fresh clone. The driving pressure throughout was the audit's discovery that "accepted" had drifted from "true," plus the parallel finding that several *deferred* ADRs cited machinery that doesn't exist.

---

### Vault / concepts & schemas

- **What:** New `code-note` note type added — 22nd type. New schema `src/.memoria/schemas/types/code-note.yaml` (`category: projects`, `gated: false`, `initial_lifecycle: proposed`, lifecycle subset `proposed → current → archived`, required `title/lifecycle/title/project/agent/task/acceptance`, `agent` enum `[codex, claude-code, other]`), folder mapping `code-note: projects` in `folders.yaml`, and a starter template `src/system/templates/code-note.md`. Docs updated: `note-types.md` (21→22 types, "Projects (2)"→"(3)"), `frontmatter.md` lifecycle-subset table adds `code-note`. **Why:** the audit found ADR-07 (code-agent attachment) PARTIAL — "Fully wired (memoria-engineer profile, `claude-code`/`codex` external agents, `code`-lane override), but the ADR's 'Files affected' promises a `system/templates/code-note.md` starter template that does not exist." The plan chose create-over-drop as "the cheaper-to-defend choice and the profile/lane wiring already exists" (`tmp/exec-plan-0.1.0-alpha.6.md` WS-3 #627). The template is "the Engineer's handoff/provenance note for external coding agents under a project's `code/` scratch" (`note-types.md`).

- **What:** `thesis.yaml` gains optional `promoted_at: date` and `promoted_by: str`; `frontmatter.md` documents them as "Promotion provenance for a thesis. A `thesis` at `lifecycle: current` **must** carry `promoted_at`." **Why:** ADR-78 (thesis note type) was PARTIAL — "ADR-78 requires 'the schema must reject a born-`current` thesis' and a review-gated promotion to `current`. Neither holds: `validate_frontmatter` only checks enum membership, and `current` is a legal enum value, so a thesis authored directly at `lifecycle: current` validates clean." The fix keys enforcement on a **provenance marker** rather than history because "`validate_frontmatter` is stateless, so key on a marker, not history" (exec-plan WS-1 #621). Crucially, the alternative — adding `projects/` to `gated_prefixes` — was **rejected**: the policy gate is "path-based and content-blind … it can't tell *create-proposed* from *promote-to-current*, and it only intercepts agent `mcp_obsidian_*` writes (it misses PI promotions typed directly in Obsidian)"; a `projects/` prefix "would dry-run all `proposed`/`provisional` agent work too — which ADR-78 says to allow." Enforcement therefore lives in the **content-aware Linter/schema layer**, resolved formally in PR #647.

- **What:** `claim.yaml` gains optional `schema_version: int`; both claim templates bumped — `src/system/templates/claim.md` and `create-linked-claim.js` now emit `schema_version: 2`; documented in `frontmatter.md` and `note-types.md` ("Claim template version 2 includes `schema_version: 2`"). **Why:** ADR-10 (claim supersession) was PARTIAL — "the ADR's other guarantee — '`query` and `write` exclude superseded claims by default' — has no implementation … The promised `schema_version` bump on the claim template is also absent" (gap analysis §4). The bump versions the new default-read behavior so pre-bump notes are legible as read under the new default (release plan §6 known-limitation).

### Gate / provenance / query behavior

- **What:** Superseded claims are now excluded **by default** from claim query and write-assist surfaces. `link-claim.js` adds `isSupersededClaim()` and skips any `notes/claims/` file with a non-empty `superseded_by` when ranking link suggestions. `AGENTS.md` gains a standing instruction: "When querying or writing from claim notes, exclude claims with non-empty `superseded_by` by default. Include superseded claims only when the task explicitly asks for lineage, audit, or supersession history." Reflected in `frontmatter.md` and `note-types.md`. **Why:** closes the missing half of ADR-10. Design constraint recorded as a known-limitation: "this changes default read behavior, and notes authored before the claim `schema_version` bump are read under the new default" (release plan §6). Chosen as default-on-but-overridable so lineage/audit tasks can still opt in.

- **What:** Confirmed (no code change) that the deterministic Project-gate materialization is **not** a policy-gate regression. **Why:** the born-`current`/promotion enforcement decision raised the question of whether gating `projects/` would break gate materialization; the exec-plan retired it by verifying `structural_impact.py:743` "writes `project-gate-index.md` via direct `write_text` (zero obsidian-MCP), so it bypasses the policy gate entirely" (PR #647 body; exec-plan WS-1 #621).

- **What:** Runtime Obsidian-MCP TLS conformance re-verified and installer/profile HTTPS verification added (Track A #620, PR #651). Repo source already used `https://127.0.0.1:${OBSIDIAN_MCP_PORT}/mcp` + `ssl_verify: ${OBSIDIAN_MCP_SSL_VERIFY}`; alpha.6 adds fresh-deploy verification that generated profiles carry HTTPS + `ssl_verify`. **Why:** ADR-31 was the audit's single 🔴 finding — "the deployed runtime contradicts it … all five `~/.hermes/profiles/*/config.yaml` serve `http://…/mcp` with no `ssl_verify` … So `OBSIDIAN_API_KEY` rides unencrypted loopback in production" (gap analysis §1). The prior profile comment ("Hermes can't skip TLS verify … hence plain HTTP") was proven **wrong**: "Hermes feeds `ssl_verify` to httpx's `verify` (`mcp_tool.py:1355,1443`), which accepts a CA-bundle path, so the exported self-signed PEM verifies cleanly" — a runtime-config fix, no code change (PR #647). This is the one High-priority security blocker of the release; live-sandbox HTTPS smoke (S4) stayed tracked in release issues, not code.

### Pipeline / ingest / enrichment

- No pipeline/extraction/enrichment design changes shipped. The **shadow/instrument telemetry harvest** (ADR-38 pre-file similarity ratchet #370, ADR-65 shadow proposers #611, ADR-66 instrument #416, ADR-35 misfire sweep #371) was explicitly **deferred to alpha.7**. **Why:** "their telemetry has no corpus to chew on until the Phase-1 harness can seed one … two of them run over claim/paper notes that don't exist on a clean scaffold, so they measure nothing until the Phase-1 harness can seed a corpus. Deferring them to alpha.7 is the cheapest value-per-hour cut" (release plan §5, exec-plan Scope).
- **What:** ADR-20 publication-path capture signals (`disposition.jsonl`/`cost.jsonl`) documented as an **upstream-Hermes known-limitation (#625), not a gate**. **Why:** "stay empty because Hermes doesn't yet surface the card `metadata` overlay … the exporter is already wired to emit the moment it appears" (gap analysis §5; release plan §6). Ships as documented limitation because the blocker is external.

### Retrieval / derived store

- No new retrieval subsystem. The default superseded-claim filter (above) is the one behavior change touching the write-assist/query surface.

### Discovery / UI / navigation

- **What:** Project becomes a **first-class gate surface inside the Studio workspace** — *not* a fourth saved workspace (Track A #622, PR #653). Added: QuickAdd command `Memoria: open Project gate` + `src/system/scripts/open-project-gate.js` (loads the Studio workspace, then opens `system/dashboards/project-gate.md`); a Project-gate button and `[!suggestions]` callout in `home.md`; a "Project gate" section in `studio.md` embedding `project-gate.base#Active projects`. `workspaces.json` still registers only Desk/Library/Studio (verified — no fourth workspace). Docs: `dashboards.md` now says "Project gate opens inside Studio," Studio's stale "Project workflow stays deferred to alpha.4/alpha.3" copy removed. **Why:** ADR-70 (fourth navigation gate) + ADR-77 (project gate) were both PARTIAL on the same missing surface — "the deterministic Project-gate logic is fully built and tested … `project-gate.{md,base}` exist. But … `workspaces.json` registers only Desk/Library/Studio. The gate is reachable by link but is not a switchable top-level workspace" (gap analysis §3). The design deliberately avoids reviving a fourth saved workspace: "Studio and Project are two names for the same workspace: Studio is the saved workspace shell, and Project is the bounded-inquiry gate surface opened inside it" (exec-plan WS-2; script header comment). The custom `registerBasesView` pilot stays deferred (ADR-77), so the gate "renders through the standard surface."

- **What:** `home.md` dashboard reorganization — Studio moved out of "Agent ops" into a new "Project — bounded inquiry" `[!suggestions]` group alongside the Project Gate link. **Why:** follows the Project-gate-inside-Studio model so Home's navigation reflects Studio as the drafting shell where the gate opens.

- **What:** `dashboards.md` count/description corrections — clarified 16 rows = 4 workspace landing surfaces (Desk/Library/Studio/Project) + 12 standalone health dashboards; audit-log corrected from "current week" to "recent writes (each view row-capped, not time-windowed)." **Why:** verified-consistency pass — "dashboards.md: 'twelve / not different inventories' → 16 rows = 12 health dashboards + 4 workspace gate surfaces"; "audit-log: not week-scoped (views are row-capped) — corrected" (commit 4a54c13f body).

### Distribution / evaluation — the test-env harness (ADR-80 Phase 1)

- **What:** New **model-free L0–L4 golden-path test harness** (Track B #586, PR #655). `scripts/test_env_harness.py` replays a version-controlled cassette (`fixtures/test-env/cassettes/alpha6-l4-golden-path.json`) against a disposable vault, driving deterministic Memoria operations and asserting artifact shape, schema validity, the Project gate, and the policy deny path. Cassettes match on **tool name + argument shape, not raw prompt text** ("catches wiring and schema drift while staying stable across prompt wording changes"). Wired into `scripts/e2e-smoke.sh`; pytest coverage added; new reusable procedure `docs/testing/plans/test-env-harness-plan.md`. An **opt-in `model-smoke` command** exists but is skipped unless `MEMORIA_MODEL_BASE_URL` is set. **Why:** ADR-80's own phasing — "Memoria's load-bearing logic is deterministic (Operations, the policy gate, ingest, schemas), so the model layer and the visual layer … buy the *last* increment of confidence, not the first." Phase 1 is "~20% of the cost, ~80% of the value." The key design move — L4 belongs in the model-free phase — was argued from ADR-29: "ADR-29 draws its cheap/expensive line at the L4/L5 boundary — L0-L4 are wiring, L5 is quality … The agent steps need a model only to emit a structurally-valid output, which a seed or a recording supplies, so the model is needed at record time, not run time" (commit aada1dff body; ADR-80 Phased-adoption §). The literature/online-research bet: "Gemma 4 12B is GA … official GGUF … served by `llama-server --jinja` over `/v1`," which resolved ADR-80's model-existence gate 2 and narrowed gate 3 to a ~5-min smoke (commit 06de3f66 body).

- **What:** The G3 `model-smoke` was fixed to use `tool_choice: "auto"` (not a forced function), `max_tokens` raised to 128, request timeout made configurable via `MEMORIA_MODEL_TIMEOUT` (default 90s) (commit 6348ca7f, PR #662). **Why:** "Several local OpenAI-compatible runtimes (e.g. Ollama serving Gemma) return empty output when a function is forced, but emit a correct tool_call under `tool_choice: auto` — so the smoke could never pass against the intended local model … a large model on CPU can take ~45s for a single tool call." Verified live: qwen2.5:7b on Ollama → PASS in 3.4s.

- **What:** New static **plugin provenance lock manifest** `src/.obsidian/plugin-provenance-lock.json` — pins version, upstream repo, `pinned_ref`, per-file SHA-256, license, and `local_patch_status` for the 12 vendored plugins; plus `tests/test_plugin_provenance.py` (Track A #585, PR #649). **Why:** ADR-74 (plugin provenance manifest) was deferred but its static-lock slice was "mechanical, no external dependency … 12 vendored plugins under `src/.obsidian/plugins/`, zero SHA/license manifest today" (cadence-review Tier A). Ships as a **precursor** while ADR-74 stays deferred: the manifest's own `notes` field records "Updater and CI provenance-doctor remain deferred; this lock pins the checked-in artifact hashes for manual audit" (release plan §6 known-limitation).

### Security

- The ADR-31 HTTPS conformance work (above) is the release's security headline — closing the plain-loopback bearer-token regression.
