**What:** **Fresh-workspace-only initialization; no migration path** (`_notes/…design.md` §20; installer skeleton in `folders.yaml`). — **Why:** §20 "There is no alpha.11 system installed outside the sandbox, so alpha.11 has **no migration, upgrade path, backwards-compatibility mode, or cutover** … do not map legacy records." §7.1 table repeatedly: "Created only by the alpha.11 capture pipeline in the sandbox; no legacy records are mapped."

**What:** Docs restructured to Diátaxis around the model spine; retired the entire `docs/testing/plans/` and per-release `docs/releasing/0.1.0-alpha.{1,2,3,5,6,7,8,9,10}/` folders (many `D` entries in the docs diff; commits `285e67e1`, `33e72f43`, `ad9bfd22`, `5de7afbe`). — **Why:** commit `ad9bfd22` "retire testing and release folders"; `285e67e1` "Redesign docs around model spine"; §Documentation-and-release-record ADR cluster: "system documentation, ADRs, release plan, and `tmp/` disposition are part of the alpha.11 definition of done; `tmp/` scratch is not a durable source of truth." A live docs link checker was added (commit `4b71a4d5`) and derived schema/profile reference pages made generator-owned (commit `1472b529`).

---

### Security

**What:** Prompt-injection is now a first-class detection + provenance-checkpoint surface: `integrity-prompt-injection-check` (detect) + `integrity-provenance-checkpoint` (route uncorroborated-source synthesis to PI) (`vault-template/capabilities/operations/`; §12). — **Why:** §12 residual-risk section: structural checks "**not** a crafted injection or a well-formed-but-unwarranted claim" → the design "**does not assume detection works**" and "**re-introduces gating where recall is low**" via "a **provenance-triggered human checkpoint on injection-prone content**." This is "the single risk most likely to force a gate back in."

**What:** Capability-import supply-chain vetting shipped as the `ai-catalog.json` `trust` manifest + quarantine-not-run rule (`vault-template/capabilities/ai-catalog.json`; §12). — **Why:** §12 "Importing a `capabilities/` bundle brings in untrusted **code/instructions the agents will execute** … a higher-stakes surface than untrusted *content*. Alpha vetting = content hashes + source repo + quarantine + **SPDX license IDs** … in-toto/SLSA … are the **deferred upgrade**."

**What:** Agent-rendered UI rule codified (declarative, catalog-bound component set; no raw HTML/JS) even though the plugin catalog is deferred (§12; §8.1). — **Why:** §12 "**Agent-rendered UI is declarative and catalog-bound** … **never raw HTML/JS from an agent**, which is a code-execution / injection vector. The catalog is deferred with the plugin; the *rule* holds now."

**What:** Retired the old policy-MCP gated-write enforcement as the security boundary; the boundary is now channel-separation + tool allowlists + no-exfil + trusted-writer-only commits (`operation.yaml` `allowed_tools`/`allowed_paths`/`allowed_network`; §12; old ADR-27 deleted). — **Why:** §12 "agents never commit canonical files or the journal — only the worker commits, and agent code execution is read-only/mechanical … Perplexity-based cleaning … is **ingest hygiene … not a security control** — the security boundary is channel separation + tool allowlists + no-exfil."

---

### ADRs — the mass-retirement event

**What:** One implicit reset supersedes an obsolete ADR set; **~30 ADRs deleted** and **1 added** (ADR-121). Deleted (design-bearing): `01-three-layer-architecture`, `02-seven-specialist-profiles`, `04-lifecycle-over-topic-folders`, `08-typed-relations-frontmatter`, `13-homepage-front-door`, `17-shared-candidate-frontmatter`, `18-rename-agent-verdict`, `27-hermes-native-config-and-gate-enforcement`, `34-code-artifact-autopilot`, `36-dedicated-review-note-type`, `37-retriever-scout-profile`, `40-admin-gui-surface`, `42-profile-compilation`, `45-release-management-model`, `58-adjacent-tool-integrations`, `59-classical-method-displacements`, `60-cross-vault-knowledge-sharing`, `61-nightly-discovery-loop`, `63-multi-machine-deployment`, `65-retrieval-and-schema-extensions`, `67-drift-procedures`, `68-workspaces-desk-library-studio`, `76-versioned-vault-release`, `82-four-gates-canonical-vocabulary`, `84-read-only-obsidian-inspector`, `85-todoist-gap-card-mirroring`, `86-open-design-deliverable-rendering-agent`, `87-static-html-admin-reports` (commits `332cd930` "Retire stale ADRs", `051494af` "Prune retired ADR records", `1c745c7d`). — **Why:** §19 "**The reset is a mass-retirement event:** one *reset* ADR supersedes the obsolete set en masse; these clusters are written **current-state, self-contained, no history/lineage prose** … History lives in superseded ADRs + releasing notes, not in the live set." Each deletion maps to a retired design pillar: three-layer arch → five-plane stack (§8); seven profiles → operation policy (§11); lifecycle-over-topic-folders → OKF bundle roots + check_status (§6); typed-relations → typed Links predicate set (§5); homepage → launch screen (§8.1); shared-candidate-frontmatter / dedicated-review-note-type → one `note` type (§5); code-artifact-autopilot → deferred code lane (§11/§15); admin-gui / static-html-admin → declarative catalog-bound UI (§12); nightly-discovery / cross-vault / multi-machine → deferred scope (§16); four-gates-vocabulary → single thin export gate (§4.5).

**What (retained/reshaped):** ADR-107 (OKF interchange bundle format) updated, ADR-116 (Obsidian surface architecture), ADR-118 (dashboard consolidation), ADR-119 (schema-driven document creation) updated, ADR-121 added (`docs/adr/`). — **Why:** these are the surviving spine of the new model — OKF substrate (§6), Obsidian surface (§8.1), dashboards (§8.1), and the enqueue-only control-panel boundary (ADR-121 ↔ §8.1). ADR-03 (structural-review-gate) and ADR-50 (universal-lifecycle-and-maturity) were **not deleted** but marked `nav_exclude` and left with stale gated-zone/maturity prose — an intentional "history lives in superseded ADRs" posture, but worth flagging as residual drift against the shipped `check_status` model (this is inference from the `nav_exclude` edit + surviving `notes/claims/` references in ADR-03, not documented as a deliberate contradiction).

---

### Removed / retired (summary, with why)

- **Per-write approval + review-gated folders** (`gated_prefixes`) → retired for the `check_status` read-barrier: per-atom approval "checks the wrong object" and rubber-stamps under load (§2, Jacobs 2021).
- **`maturity` (seedling/budding/evergreen) + universal `lifecycle`** → retired: "trust = the checks" (§5); consumption eligibility is `check_status`, not a human-set maturity.
- **Durable Inbox card Concepts** (candidate/gap/flag/alert/work-prompt/worker-card/worklist-item) → retired: attention is a **generated projection** over journal/check/queue state (§8.2, §17).
- **Profiles / fleet / five-lane runtime** → retired: policy binds to operations, not identity (§11, §17).
- **Hermes as control-plane** (session DB, memory, Kanban, cron, goals as source of truth) → demoted to a specialized library adapter (§8.2, §11, §13; ADR-22/27 deleted).
- **Separate `paper`/`dataset`/`repository`/`code-note`/`thesis` types** → collapsed into `source.item_type` and the single `project` type (§5, §7.1).
- **CEBM `evidence_level`, `entity`-pointer source notes, mandatory `claim.sources`** → replaced by `csl_json` + typed Links + `evidence_set` warrant (§7.1).
- **Embedded `creation:` form blocks inside type schemas** → moved to QuickAdd/Modal-Form scripts + generated forms (schema-driven creation, ADR-119); schemas now declare only shape/enums.
- **The bundled `mediterranean-diet` sample skeleton** (old `folders.yaml` `.memoria/samples/…`) → removed: alpha.11 seeds "only test projects and captured sources created through the alpha.11 pipeline" (§20).
- **Full ARD federated discovery, RO-Crate/BagIt, external MCP exposure, in-toto/SLSA, draft/verify/export, code-lane autonomy** → explicitly **deferred** (not retired): boundary/scope decisions in §11/§13/§15/§16, kept as named future work so the alpha stays "the basic knowledge cycle, end to end, with the plugin."

## alpha.12 — The SQLite state boundary: working-state becomes a real database, the keep-set stays plain markdown

**Theme:** alpha.12 relaxes the alpha.11 "files-are-SSOT everywhere" rule and installs a **single embedded SQLite database (`.memoria/state/memoria.sqlite`) as the source of truth for Memoria's *working state*** — the operation queue/request envelope, the hash-chained journal, the catalog of sources, the concept/output ledger, durable materialization payloads, and the machine-consumer read barrier — while the **keep-set (`knowledge/` + `capabilities/` + generated `references.bib`) remains git-tracked markdown**. The release was driven by a single sharp reframing ("the keep-test": *what must survive Memoria's death is markdown OKF + a portable bibliography; everything else is free to be SQLite*), and by four disposable pre-implementation spikes whose **three FAIL verdicts** forced concrete contract decisions before any engine code was written. This is a storage/persistence/recovery release: the design also re-frames the whole system as a **CLI-first standalone integrity engine with pluggable triggers** (command / file-change / schedule) rather than an Obsidian app, though the shipped code lands only the engine spine and cross-store recovery, not the full trigger/CLI surface.

A caveat that runs through this changelog: the alpha.12 **design doc is far larger than what shipped in this commit range.** The design specifies an `entities`/`catalog_links` graph, field-provenance, enrichment runs, recursive-CTE cascade-rollback, a git-tracked `journal-heads.jsonl` anchor, and a Turso backup adapter — but the shipped `state.py` lands a deliberately smaller 7-table schema + 1 view, plus cross-store recovery. I mark design-only items as such.

---

### Vault / concepts / schemas

- **What:** Every keep-set Concept type gained an optional `citations: list` field — `digest.yaml`, `hub.yaml`, and `note.yaml` each added `citations` to their `optional:` block (`vault-template/.memoria/schemas/types/{digest,hub,note}.yaml`), surfaced in `docs/reference/document-types.md` and `frontmatter.md`. **Why:** this is the load-bearing consequence of moving the catalog into SQLite. Once source identity lives in a database that is *not* part of the takeout promise, a note/digest/hub that only holds a `source_id` handle becomes meaningless the moment SQLite is dropped. The design's §1 self-sufficiency invariant demands the keep-set "still read as complete, grounded knowledge in any markdown/OKF tool" after deleting SQLite, so §3's **Cross-store reference rule** requires denormalizing a compact survival copy (`source_id`, `title`, `authors`, `issued`, and at least one of `doi`/`url`/`citekey`) into the file itself: "`source_id` is the live handle; the embedded Citation is the survival copy" (`0.1.0-alpha.12-design.md` §3). The cross-store spike's FAIL result ("Cross-store same-operation citation lifecycle") corroborated that citations must be first-class, not derived on demand.

- **What:** Two new workspace skeleton directories — `.memoria/state/` (holds `memoria.sqlite`) and `.memoria/audit/` (git-trackable audit anchors) — added to `folders.yaml` `skeleton:` (skeleton entries `32 → 34`, reflected in `docs/reference/configuration.md`), each with a tracked `.gitkeep`; `.gitignore` now ignores `.memoria/state/**` contents while keeping the directory. **Why:** SQLite needs a durable, per-machine, gitignored home distinct from the disposable worker mirrors (`index/`, `queue/`, `staging/`, `quarantine/`), because the DB is *authoritative* working state, not a rebuildable index — "runtime content is disposable" no longer applies to it (`vault-template/.gitignore`, `on-disk-layout.md`: "`state/` — SQLite working-state DB"). The `audit/` directory scaffolds §7's git-tracked journal-head anchor (tamper-evidence for the SQLite journal). **Note:** in this commit range `audit/` is only *created*; the `journal-heads.jsonl` write path described in design §7 is not yet wired (the anchor helper appears only in later versions).

- **What:** `concepts.concept_type` is constrained to a fixed 13-value enum in the DB — `source, digest, note, hub, capability, operation, skill, mcp, workflow, person, organization, venue, project` (`state.py` `_init`). **Why:** this is the DB half of the "generator ≠ checker / prevent-what-a-DB-can" split (design §4): concept typing becomes a `CHECK` constraint the worker transaction enforces, converting a class of type errors "from detection to prevention." The through-line remains `.memoria/schemas/types/*.yaml` as the Concept-field owner; the SQLite enum is a role adapter checked against it (§2/§5).

### Retrieval / store / persistence — the SQLite state boundary (the core of the release)

- **What:** A new 763-line module **`src/memoria_vault/runtime/state.py`** introduces the SQLite working-state boundary at `.memoria/state/memoria.sqlite` (`DB_REL`), created via `connect()` with `PRAGMA foreign_keys = ON`, initialized by an inlined `executescript` schema (`SCHEMA_VERSION` not yet externalized — the standalone `schema.sql` file arrives in a later release). Shipped tables: `operation_requests`, `journal_events`, `concepts`, `outputs`, `materialization_payloads`, `catalog_sources`, `derivations`; plus the `consumable_outputs` view. **Why:** alpha.11's "passive rebuilt index over files" could never *prevent* violations, only detect them post-hoc. The design's clean-slate DB role (§4) makes SQLite "the SSOT for catalog and ops, and the projection engine for search/derived views," giving four jobs: retrieval, catalog+ops SSOT, relational/graph queries, and **write-boundary constraints** (FK/UNIQUE/CHECK/DAG "inside the same worker transaction"). The driving reframe: the keep-test proved most of Memoria's state (queue, journal, catalog graph, flags) fails the "need-this-to-think-outside-Memoria" test, so it "is free to be SQLite" (§1). Rejected alternatives are named explicitly: SQLite-as-SSOT-for-the-keep-set, CRDTs, and a hosted primary DB are all rejected because "the keep-set remains plain markdown; CRDT/hosted-primary storage breaks the local single-user simplicity target" (§4); a Python `eventsourcing` framework is rejected because "SQLite transactions, ordinary tables, and a small recovery state machine are clearer for a single-user local tool" (§7). **Note (design vs shipped):** the design's `entities`, `catalog_links`, field-provenance, and enrichment tables did **not** ship in this range — the catalog is a single flat `catalog_sources` table; the source↔entity↔link graph is design-only for alpha.12.

- **What:** The **request envelope** is now a durable SQLite row. `state.request_envelope(...)` builds and `save_request()` persists a uniform envelope with `request_id`, `trigger_type` (CHECK-constrained to `command`/`file_change`/`schedule`), `operation_id`, `args`, `idempotency_key` (UNIQUE), `target_path`, `target_hash`, `causal_refs`, `actor`, `provenance`, and optional `schedule_id`; `operation_requests.status` is CHECK-constrained to `pending`/`running`/`done`/`failed` (`state.py` `_init`, `save_request`). The worker (`worker.py`) now writes this envelope on every `enqueue_trusted_write`/`enqueue_operation`, deduplicates against SQLite first (`state.request_job`), and claims the next job from SQLite (`state.next_pending_job` → `_claim_sqlite_job`), mirroring JSON files under `.memoria/queue/{pending,running,done,failed}` only for Obsidian compatibility. **Why:** design §6's **Trigger lifecycle — one request envelope**: "Every trigger creates the same durable operation request before the worker runs" so "the queue survives a crash" (the `requested` state "makes accepted work durable"). The §11 gates "Trigger unification" and "Request-envelope contract" require command/file-change/schedule triggers to persist identical fields and enter the same lifecycle. The `idempotency_key UNIQUE` constraint enforces the design's crash-safe, replay-safe queue. Making the queue a DB row rather than a directory of JSON files is what lets "SQLite decide what to resume, roll back, or re-promote" on crash (§4).

- **What:** The **journal is now an append-only, hash-chained SQLite table.** `journal_events(event_id, timestamp, event_type, machine, payload_json, prev_hash, row_hash UNIQUE)` with `prev_hash`/`row_hash` chaining (`GENESIS` seed, SHA-256 over the row) and two `BEFORE UPDATE`/`BEFORE DELETE` triggers that `RAISE(ABORT, 'journal is append-only')`. Every trusted-writer event is now dual-written: `_append_event` appends to the JSONL journal **and** `state.append_journal_event` (`trusted_writer.py`). **Why:** design §7 rejects verifiable-log servers (immudb / Trillian / Sigstore-Rekor) as "overkill and break local-first," choosing instead "a local append-only SQLite journal (`event_id`, `prev_hash`, `row_hash`, append-only triggers)" for "enough practical tamper-evidence for the single-user threat model." The **SQLite journal-integrity spike** proved append-only rows and hash chains "need an external git-tracked head anchor for tamper-evidence" (design Provenance / test-results), motivating the (design-specified) `audit/` anchor. The journal vocabulary (`requested/run/model_call/derived/check-fired/checked/materialized/resolved`) is carried as the contract; the "Journal vocabulary and queue/flag projection rebuild" spike PASSED, confirming the full vocabulary can rebuild queue/flag/status views (test-results §PASS).

- **What:** A **cross-store materialization protocol** with an explicit `materialization_status` state machine. `outputs(output_id, concept_type, store∈{db,file}, target_path, staging_path, check_status∈{unchecked,checked,quarantined}, materialization_status∈{none,pending,materialized,failed}, output_sha256, materialized_commit, failure_reason)`, paired with `materialization_payloads(output_id PK→outputs ON DELETE CASCADE, expected_sha256, payload_text)`. `stage_concept` now calls `state.record_file_output(...)` storing the **full staged payload text** plus its hash (rejecting empty payloads and hash mismatches); `_write_checked` calls `state.mark_checked(...)`; and `commit_writer_changes` calls `state.mark_materialized(rel, commit=<hash>)` for each committed path (`trusted_writer.py`). **Why:** this is the release's trickiest correctness surface. Design §4/§6 make the rule "**Transactions: SQLite first, file promotion second**" — a DB commit can land before git promotion finishes, so file-owned outputs stay `materialization_status: pending` and non-consumable until the coupled git commit records its hash and flips to `materialized`. The **persistence/crash-replay spike FAILED** with the decisive finding: "Hash-only derived events cannot replay materialization after staging is lost… hashes alone are insufficient" (test-results §FAIL "Persistence authority and crash replay"). That failure is what forced the `materialization_payloads` table to store the **actual payload bytes**, not just a hash — design §92: "Hash-only pending rows are invalid… the DB stores the staged payload bytes." The lifecycle spike also proved "`checked` must be a check result rather than a consumability state" (design Provenance), which is why `check_status` and `materialization_status` are two independent columns.

- **What:** **Crash recovery from durable payloads.** `state.recover_pending_materializations()` scans file-owned outputs that are `checked` but still `pending`; if the target file already exists on disk with the expected hash it flips to `materialized`, otherwise it replays the file from the durable `payload_text` (failing the row with a `failure_reason` if the payload is missing or hash-mismatched). Wired to a new `memoria worker recover` CLI command (`worker.py` `main`). **Why:** directly answers the §11 "Crash/materialization replay" gate and the WP1 accept criterion ("crash *after* DB commit replays file promotion from payloads; hash-only pending rows rejected"). It is the concrete mechanism behind design §6's "on crash, the worker resumes promotion from the durable materialization payload or marks the operation failed." **Note:** the shipped recovery is payload-replay only; the design's git-commit-verification step (`_committed_materialization_commit`) and `recover_running_requests` appear only in later versions.

- **What:** The **read barrier is now a SQL view.** `consumable_outputs` selects outputs where `check_status='checked'` AND (`store='db'` OR (`store='file'` AND `materialization_status='materialized'`)). **Why:** design §6 makes the read barrier "a *machine-consumer* guarantee": agents/retrieval/export consume only this view, and "`checked` alone is never enough for file-owned outputs." The **checked-barrier spike PASSED**, confirming machine output stays outside `knowledge/` until checked promotion while "PI live edit can exist in knowledge while machine consumers filter it out" (test-results §PASS) — the human is trusted and reads live content directly; the barrier gates machines, not people (design §6, carried from `why-review-gate-is-structural` / `why-human-gate` principles).

- **What:** A **`derivations(input_id, output_id, actor∈{pi,operation,integrity})`** edge table, populated by `record_file_output` from each output's declared inputs. **Why:** this is the rollback-graph substrate. Design §4/§6 want "cascade-rollback blast-radius and retraction propagation" as "recursive CTEs… not hand-rolled walks," and §4 job 3 makes "Concepts/Links/journal as tables" so "transitive closure becomes SQL." The **SQLite oracle + recursive-rollback spike PASSED** ("UNIQUE, FK, type enum, DAG check, and recursive blast-radius query all worked… blast radius spans DB and file-backed concepts via the journal projection," test-results §PASS). **Note (design vs shipped):** alpha.12 lands the `derivations` edges but **not** the recursive-CTE cascade-rollback operation itself — rollback still runs through the alpha.11 integrity/journal path in this commit range.

### Pipeline / ingest / catalog / enrichment

- **What:** The **catalog is now SQLite-authoritative.** `catalog_sources(source_id PK, concept_path, doi UNIQUE, title, resource, identifiers_json, citekey, csl_json, metadata_status∈{verified,partial,unverified,not-indexed}, check_status, content_hash, raw_hash)`. `capture_source` (`capture.py`) and `_write_checked` for `type='source'` (`trusted_writer.py`) now call `state.upsert_catalog_source(...)` on every checked source, and `compile_source_digest` (`operations.py`) upserts before deriving. **Why:** design §3/§4/§10: "SQLite is SSOT for catalog + ops. File SSOT is limited to the keep-set." The `doi UNIQUE` constraint is the "no duplicate `source_id`/DOI" prevention from §4. The alpha.11 model kept source identity in per-source markdown; the keep-test judged the *relational catalog graph* as working state that fails the survival test (§1), so it moves to SQLite while the source *concept file* survives as the projection.

- **What:** **`references.bib` generation flips to SQLite-first with a file fallback, and becomes atomic with bibliography-changing captures.** `render_references_bib` now reads `state.catalog_sources(vault)` when `state.has_catalog_sources()`, falling back to scanning `catalog/sources/**/source.md` only when the DB has no rows (`capture.py`). `capture_source` computes `_has_bibliography_fields(...)` on the checked source and, when true, calls `write_references_bib(commit=False)` and folds `references.bib` into the *same* git commit and journal `outputs` list (`capture.py`). Documented across `ingest.md`, `system-actions.md`, `system-artifacts.md`, `operations.md`. **Why:** the **catalog-recovery spike FAILED** — "Periodic export loses Memoria-owned catalog changes made after the last export… Alpha.12 needs atomic tracked export per catalog commit" (test-results §FAIL "Catalog recovery from committed artifacts"). That forced design §3's **bibliography atomicity** rule: "every transaction that changes BibTeX-visible source fields schedules `references.bib` as a file-owned materialization before the operation can complete" and the §11 gate "Bibliography atomicity." `references.bib` is the **bibliography takeout** — "enough for the user to take completed sources with the keep-set" (§1) — the accepted lossy portability tradeoff vs the full catalog graph (§9 Costs: "`references.bib` is portable but lossy relative to the catalog DB; this is accepted for alpha.12 simplicity").

- **What:** **Compact citations are embedded into machine-derived digests, hubs, and note candidates.** `compile_source_digest` computes `state.compact_citation(source_rel)` and, when present, writes `citations: [citation]` into both the digest frontmatter and every derived hub frontmatter (`operations.py`); `emit_note_candidates` propagates `citations` from the source row or the parent digest into each candidate note (`knowledge.py`). `compact_citation` builds the survival map from `csl_json` (authors via `_csl_authors`, date via `_csl_issued`) and picks one locator in priority `doi > url > citekey`. **Why:** implements the §3 cross-store reference rule at the point of generation — the machine writer is responsible for making its own output self-sufficient, so "this is what makes §1's self-sufficiency invariant hold for digests and hubs, not just notes."

### Gate / provenance / integrity checks

- **What:** A new integrity check **`integrity-citation-survival-check`**: runtime helper `integrity.check_citation_survival(...)` flags any `checked` note/digest/hub whose catalog-source references lack a valid compact `citations` payload, delegating the per-frontmatter rule to `state.check_citation_payload(...)` (which requires each citation map to carry `title`, `authors`, `issued`, and one of `doi`/`url`/`citekey`). Shipped as a new capability Concept (`capabilities/operations/integrity-citation-survival-check.md`, `required_checks: [citation-survival]`, `risk_class: medium`, `runner: local`, `model: deterministic-fixture`), registered in `ai-catalog.json` and `capabilities/index.md`, added to the worker's `INTEGRITY_SWEEP_OPERATIONS` and dispatch, and documented (the daily sweep now runs **nine** integrity checks, up from eight, per `operations.md`). **Why:** the citation-survival invariant is only useful if it is *enforced*. Design §3 states "Validators reject a keep-set source reference that has no matching Citation payload," and this check is the enforcement arm — a structural, deterministic check consistent with `why-deterministic-methods` (prevent/detect only what is machine-decidable; the compact-payload presence test is fully structural).

- **What:** The **seeded-error verdict gate re-baselined to alpha.12.** New fixture `vault-template/system/eval/alpha12-seeded-errors.json` (13 seeded cases across structural/blind/checkpoint classes: evidence-resolves, contradiction-link, link-target, source-metadata ×2, stale-as-current, unwarranted-claim, crafted-injection, fresh-uncorroborated-source, poisoned-span, quote-anchor), with the release bars pinned at `recall_min=1.0`, `false_positive_rate_max=0.0`, `rollback_completeness_min=1.0`, `residual_error_rate_max=0.0`, `checkpoint_value_rate_min=1.0`. The worker's `run-seeded-error-verdict` and `seeded_errors` now prefer the alpha12 bundle and fall back to alpha11 if absent (`worker.py`; `operations.md`, `system-actions.md`). **Why:** design §8 carries forward "the gateless model + the seeded-error verdict as the release gate to real use" — the engine must be *certified* before real use (exec-plan WP9). Re-versioning the bundle keeps the gate pinned to the alpha.12 engine while the fallback preserves backward compatibility during transition. This is the concrete instrument for the two carried-forward bets (integrity engine trustworthiness; compounding-wiki value).

### Profiles / runtime — engine reframing (design intent) vs shipped

- **What (design):** The system is re-framed from "Obsidian app + worker" to a **standalone CLI-first integrity engine** with three pluggable trigger types (command / file-change scan/watch / schedule) all producing one request envelope, a pydantic-ai typed-operation runner, and Obsidian/Zotero/Hermes/MCP demoted to *optional adapters, not architectural dependencies* (design §2, §5, §10). The Co-PI interview becomes engine state (`memoria ask/answer/resume`), never a pydantic-ai session or `pydantic-graph`. **Why:** design §2 — "The engine is the product… don't make Obsidian, Zotero, Hermes, or any adapter the architecture." Heterogeneous storage "makes the engine boundary load-bearing (no trigger or surface could touch files+DB+blobs directly and stay consistent)." Rejected: workflow engines (Temporal/Prefect/Dagster/Airflow — "the worker is one queue, not a DAG orchestrator"), LangChain/LlamaIndex ("heavy framework-owned state"), and external agent-runtime ownership ("borrow useful prompt/workflow patterns, not runtime ownership") (§5, §7).

- **What (shipped subset):** The worker gained the *scaffolding* of the trigger model: `enqueue_operation`/`enqueue_trusted_write` accept `trigger_type`, `causal_refs`, `actor`, `provenance`, `schedule_id`; new CLI subcommands `scan` (enqueues a `file_change` `observe-pi-edits` pass), `run-scheduled` (enqueues a `schedule` job), and `recover`; the integrity sweep now tags its jobs `trigger_type="schedule"` (`worker.py`). **Why:** these land the §11 "Trigger unification" and "Standalone CLI" contract surface incrementally — command/file-change/schedule all funnel through `state.request_envelope`. **Note (design vs shipped):** the full pydantic-ai runner, the `memoria ask/answer/resume` interview CLI, `watch`, and the standalone `memoria <operation>` binary are **not** in this commit range — only the worker-level envelope + trigger tagging shipped. The docs still describe the Obsidian control panel as the worker's front end and note the JSON queue is mirrored "for Obsidian compatibility" (`system-artifacts.md`).

### Distribution / evaluation / security

- **What:** `.gitignore` and folder skeleton updates (above) make the SQLite DB gitignored per-machine state, and the docs now state plainly that **SQLite backup is a first-class, separate concern** from the git-backed takeout set. `on-disk-layout.md`, `configuration.md`, `operations.md` all re-labeled alpha.11 → alpha.12 with the state/audit additions. **Why:** design §3 "Backup posture (kept honest)" and §9 "Costs": "SQLite is authoritative for Memoria working state, so a full Memoria backup needs ordinary SQLite backup/snapshot handling. Alpha.12 does **not** promise full working-state portability without SQLite; it promises the user's completed knowledge and bibliography can leave." This is the honest security/durability tradeoff of the whole release, made explicit rather than hidden.

- **What (design-only, deferred):** An **optional Turso/libSQL backup/sync adapter** for the SQLite working-state DB (esp. to preserve the rollback graph and audit if the local DB is lost). **Why:** design §3/§7/§10 admit it "adds provider auth, network behavior, restore UX, compatibility limits, and free-tier/PITR terms that must be rechecked," so it is "spike-gated," "not a baseline dependency," and "not part of the ownership promise." Open question §12 D2 leaves feasibility unresolved. Nothing Turso-related shipped in this range.

- **What:** Security guardrails **carried forward unchanged** and re-affirmed: MCP-only agent sandbox (no profile ever gets file/terminal/code_execution), checks/evals pin a certified model and never route through Hermes, PI-direct-access preserved (exec-plan Guardrails). **Why:** these are alpha.11 invariants the design §8 explicitly carries; the storage rewrite must not weaken them. The write boundary stays the single choke point — "Plugin/agent/editor surfaces never write storage directly" (§6), now even more load-bearing because a surface touching files+DB+blobs directly could not stay consistent (§2).

### ADRs

- **What:** **No ADR files were added or modified in this commit range** (`docs/adr/` shows zero diff). The exec-plan's cross-cutting task — "turn §10 into ADRs — storage / engine-lifecycle / triggers-CLI / operations-runner / MCP-deferral clusters; retire the superseded alpha.11 storage/stack/operations ADRs" — was **not executed** in these commits. **Why:** not documented in the commit bodies (they are single-line: "Implement alpha.12 state boundary (#1032)"). **Inferred:** the release shipped the engine spine and its contract gates first (Phase 0 → WP1-level work) and deferred the ADR authoring/retirement, consistent with the design being explicitly labeled a "working design" that "supersedes alpha.11 §6/§8/§11" at the doc level rather than the ADR level (design §0, Provenance). The design doc itself carries the decision record for now (design §10 lists 20 settled decisions).

### Removed / retired

- **What:** The **files-SSOT-everywhere rule and the "passive rebuilt index" DB role are retired.** alpha.11's "one decision (files vs DB)" per component and "a passive rebuilt index over files" are replaced by the two-decision model (SSOT location ⟂ projection flavor) with SQLite as an intentional SSOT (design §0 table, §3). **Why:** the keep-test showed the old rule over-paid: forcing catalog/ops into many small JSON/markdown files bought no ownership benefit (they fail the survival test) while blocking real prevention, transactions, and graph queries (design §0, §9 "Buys").

- **What:** **The clean-rebuild migration target (alpha.11 §20) is retired** — alpha.12 has "**no migration target**; non-sandbox use starts from a fresh workspace" (design §0, exec-plan). **Why:** design §0 relaxes constraints for implementation simplicity; a single-machine, sandbox-only alpha with no backward-compatibility promise (§8) does not need a migration path.

- **What (design-level rejections, i.e. retired-before-adoption):** event-sourcing frameworks (`eventsourcing`), verifiable-log servers (immudb/Trillian/Sigstore-Rekor), Dolt (git-for-data SQL), policy engines (OPA/Rego, Cerbos), and workflow engines — all explicitly evaluated and rejected for the integrity core (design §7). **Why:** each is "the wrong shape" for a single-user local tool: policy engines "gate *authorization*; our gates are *knowledge-integrity* checks"; Dolt "adds a versioned-SQL engine and merge semantics the single-machine design does not need"; verifiable-log servers "solve cross-org cryptographic tamper-*proofing*" that "break local-first." The chosen posture: "the integrity core is a *thin composition over solid primitives* (SQLite + git CLI + Pydantic + NetworkX), plus the domain semantics no library provides — which is exactly the part that is the moat" (§7).

## alpha.13 — DOI catalog enrichment: capture stages, enrichment promotes

**Theme:** the multi-source scholarly enrichment subsystem lands as a worker capability on top of the alpha.12 SQLite catalog — DOI capture now stages a *durable unchecked* record and a separate `enrich-source` operation fetches Crossref/OpenAlex/Unpaywall, merges canonical CSL with per-field provenance, and is the gate that promotes a source to consumable `checked`.

**What drove this release.** The alpha.12 catalog made SQLite the working-state boundary, but `capture-source` could still promote a scholarly DOI to `checked` before any provider evidence had been fetched or reconciled — so bibliography output and retrieval could expose sources whose metadata, OA status, and *retraction state* were unverified (ADR-123 Context). alpha.13 splits capture from promotion, adds durable homes for raw content / provider payloads / provenance / blocked findings, and enforces provider etiquette through a declared allowlist. Riding alongside is a "CLI-first SSOT" documentation and decision-authority pass that makes the alpha.11–13 designs the implementation source of truth (retiring stale pre-reset ADRs and Hermes-first framing) plus a new installed-local-LLM testing tier. The cut is deliberately DOI-only and sandbox-only (`Memoria-test`), with no installed-vault migration target.

---

### Pipeline / ingest / enrichment

- **What:** Split DOI/ISBN capture from checked promotion — `capture-source` now *stages* an unchecked catalog row instead of writing a checked source. New `capture.stage_catalog_source()` writes an unchecked SQLite row + durable content/raw blobs under `.memoria/blobs/source-content/<source_id>/` and does **not** write `catalog/sources/<id>/source.md` or `references.bib`; `capture.source_requires_enrichment()` routes any input carrying a DOI/ISBN down this path, and `worker.py` dispatches accordingly (`src/memoria_vault/runtime/capture.py`, `worker.py`; manifest `vault-template/capabilities/operations/capture-source.md` gains `.memoria/blobs/source-content/` and the description "DOI/ISBN records stage for enrichment"). Non-enrichment inputs keep the alpha.12 checked-capture behavior. — **Why:** ADR-123 Decision: promoting DOI captures immediately was rejected "because checked retrieval and `references.bib` would expose sources before required provider and retraction evidence had been reconciled"; writing DOI source markdown during staging was rejected because "it recreates the catalog-frontmatter source-of-truth problem superseded by ADR-122 and leaves an unchecked source-shaped file for tools to accidentally consume." The design §1 "Capture boundary" table makes this the explicit contract.

- **What:** New `enrich-source` worker operation — the promotion gate (`src/memoria_vault/runtime/enrichment.py`, 568 new lines; new manifest `vault-template/capabilities/operations/enrich-source.md`; wired into `worker.py` and the operations table in `docs/reference/operations.md`). It loads provider config, fetches required DOI providers through the operation network allowlist, caches raw payloads, merges canonical CSL + external IDs + field provenance into SQLite, then marks the source `checked` only if required-provider and retraction checks pass. — **Why:** design §0/§3 Stage E and the exec-plan Goal: "every catalog add is enriched … merge with per-field provenance → check (incl. retraction) → commit through the alpha.12 lifecycle." Making enrichment a worker operation (not an agent tool) is a settled decision (design §8) enforcing the MCP-only sandbox — agents never get network or code-exec (ADR-32).

- **What:** Provider policy config `vault-template/.memoria/enrichment/providers.yaml` (new) — declares the `doi` branch `required: [crossref, openalex, unpaywall]`, per-provider `base_url`, `endpoint_template`, `timeout_seconds`, `rate_limit_per_second`, and `query_params` naming the `.env` variables (`OPENALEX_API_KEY`, `NCBI_EMAIL`) rather than secret values. `enrichment.provider_allowlist_issues()` fails closed if any enabled provider `base_url` is not covered by the manifest `allowed_network`. — **Why:** design §7 "One non-secret provider policy config … Actual mailto/email values and API keys live in profile `.env`, never in tracked config," and the hard rule that `providers.yaml` "is data config, not the enforcement boundary. The flat `enrich-source.md` manifest remains the hard ceiling." Keeps provider lists out of every adapter (§7) and keeps secrets untracked.

- **What:** Three provider adapters implemented inline (Crossref, OpenAlex, Unpaywall) — thin per-provider fetch + normalize, each writing a content-addressed blob under `.memoria/blobs/provider-payloads/`, a `provider_payloads` DB row, and an `api_call` journal event (provider, endpoint, request, `response_hash`, status, `latency_ms`) (`enrichment.py` `_provider_payload`/`_write_provider_blob`/`_normalize_provider`). No provider class hierarchy. — **Why:** design §8 "MVP starts with DOI required providers. Implement Crossref, OpenAlex, and Unpaywall first … No provider class hierarchy until duplicated code makes it smaller"; exec-plan "Six adapters + one reconciler; add an abstraction only when a 7th demands it." Each call as a journal `api_call` event satisfies §6 provenance ("every field is traceable to who supplied it").

- **What:** Deterministic field-authority merge + per-field provenance (`enrichment._merge_doi_source`) — Crossref is authoritative for title/authors/issued/DOI/container/type; Unpaywall for `oa_location`/license; OpenAlex supplies the OpenAlex ID and external IDs. Each canonical field records a `_provenance(field_path, value, winning_provider)` row via `state.replace_field_provenance()`. — **Why:** design §3 Stage C field-authority table and §8 "Field-authority merge with per-field provenance; high-authority conflicts → flag + `metadata_status`, never silent." Top risk in the exec-plan: "Provider disagreement — never silently pick a winner on a critical field."

- **What:** Conflict + retraction gate blocks promotion (`enrichment._is_retracted`, `_title_conflict`, `_blocked_status`) — a retracted/contested Crossref record → `blocked_status = "contested"`, a high-authority Crossref/OpenAlex title mismatch → `needs_human`; either sets `check_status = unchecked` + `metadata_status = unverified`, records a `check-fired`/failed integrity finding, and never materializes `references.bib`. — **Why:** design §6 "Retraction is never silently swallowed … blocked at the alpha.12 consumable read barrier unless explicit human resolution," and §3 Stage D conflict handling. ADR-123: "Provider failure, provider conflict, or retraction/contested evidence leaves the source unchecked … and writes a PI-reviewable attention projection under `inbox/`."

- **What:** PI-reviewable attention projections on blocked enrichment (`enrichment._write_attention_flag` → `inbox/`) — required-provider miss, provider conflict, and retraction each produce one attention file linking the source and the exact blocked check, committed via the trusted writer. — **Why:** design §3 "Human-confirmation cases produce an attention item that links the source row, candidate identifiers, provider evidence, and the exact blocked check. They do not silently become checked"; §9 "Human attention" gate. Because there is no PI catalog edit UI in this cut (ADR-121/106), attention projections are the only human-review surface.

- **What:** `references.bib` materialized from durable replay data *after* required providers pass, inside the same worker commit (`enrichment.py` renders via `capture.render_references_bib`, records the projection payload through `state.record_projection_output`, then commits). Rendering now reads checked SQLite catalog rows first, source Concepts only as fallback. — **Why:** design §1 Capture-boundary table and §9 "References materialization" gate: "citation metadata and the expected `references.bib` payload/hash are committed to SQLite first; the operation completes only after file promotion records the git commit" — the alpha.12 crash-recovery barrier. ADR-122 Consequence: "`references.bib` renders from checked SQLite catalog rows."

- **What (docs):** `docs/reference/ingest.md` rewritten around the capture/enrich split — new pipeline rows for "DOI/ISBN staging," "DOI enrichment," and "Provider policy"; read-barrier now excludes "unchecked staged catalog rows, provider payloads, source-content blobs"; deferred-work list swaps "identifier lookup" for "ISBN URL-depth enrichment … Semantic Scholar, PubMed, arXiv, graph enrichment, embeddings, and UI." — **Why:** cli-first-ssot plan §1 requires docs to "describe only implemented behavior"; the deferral list mirrors design §10 MVP cut.

### Gate / provenance / data model

- **What:** Four new SQLite tables on the alpha.12 §3 ER model (`src/memoria_vault/runtime/state.py`): `external_ids` (generic `owner_type/owner_id/namespace/value/source_provider/confidence`), `enrichment_runs` (`enrichment_status`, `required_provider_policy`, timestamps), `provider_payloads` (`run_id/provider/request_key/request_params_hash/status/raw_hash/raw_path/normalized_json/latency_ms`), and `field_provenance` (`source_id/field_path/value_hash/winning_provider/…`); plus two additive columns on `catalog_sources` (`content_path`, `raw_path`) via `_ensure_column`. New helpers `start/finish_enrichment_run`, `store_provider_payload`, `replace_external_ids`, `replace_field_provenance`, `record_projection_output`, `catalog_source`. — **Why:** design §5 data-model additions ("generic ID rows, not one schema column per provider" so future namespaces need no migration) and §2/§4 identity model. exec-plan interface note: "SQLite schema changes should be additive and idempotent … no production-vault migration target."

- **What:** Idempotency + provenance replay contract — enrichment run keyed `enrich-source:{source_id}:{hash(doi)}`, provider payloads keyed `(source_id, provider, request_key, request_params_hash)`, raw payloads content-addressed so identical inputs yield identical canonical CSL + provenance. — **Why:** design §6 Idempotency/Concurrency and §9 "Merge determinism: identical provider payloads → identical canonical record + provenance." Enables the "drop SQLite → re-enrich/rebuild" replay in the exec-plan WP5 accept criterion.

- **What:** Identity via external IDs, not name strings (`external_ids` + `_openalex_external_ids`, `_external_id`) — `authored_by`/entity edges carry DOI/OpenAlex/ORCID/ROR/ISSN namespaces. — **Why:** design §4 solves the alpha.12 `sources ↔ authors` gap: "global, stable disambiguation instead of fragile local string matching," preserving prior human merges on re-enrich (ties to the alpha.12 author-reconcile gate).

### Vault / concepts / on-disk layout

- **What:** New blob store directories + `.gitignore` and installer skeleton entries — `.memoria/blobs/provider-payloads/` and `.memoria/blobs/source-content/` (with `.gitkeep`), added to `vault-template/.gitignore` (payload contents ignored, skeleton dirs tracked) and to `folders.yaml` `skeleton`. — **Why:** design §5/§7 content-addressed cache: raw captured content and provider payloads "live in the content-addressed blob store under `.memoria/blobs/`; catalog rows store hashes/pointers" — cheap reproducible re-runs, large regenerable data never committed.

- **What:** New transient `inbox/` root — added to `folders.yaml` `transient_prefixes` and documented in `on-disk-layout.md` as "transient attention projections, not Concepts." — **Why:** ADR-119 (rewrite): "Inbox cards are not durable Concept types … They are generated attention projections over Concept and operational state." Gives blocked-enrichment attention items a declared home that converges to resolved/archived and leaves active views.

- **What (design recommendation, deferred):** design §1 records a clean-slate Concept model (records vs Concepts vs manifests vs projections; four Markdown Concept types `digest/note/hub/project`; universal frontmatter with `id/standing/links{}`), a role-first `knowledge/` keep-set (`digests/notes/hubs/projects`, `_views/`), and a kind-first directory-per-capability manifest layout (`capabilities/<kind>/<name>/capability.md`, `_generated/`). **None enforced in alpha.13.** — **Why:** design §8/§10 explicitly defer these: "Alpha.13 MVP keeps flat operation manifests … Keep current generated projection paths, including tracked `capabilities/ai-catalog.json`." The design note frames them as targets requiring "a separate structural ADR/PR before promotion," per the "simplest design that meets the requirement" discipline and to avoid migration churn on a DOI-only cut.

### Distribution / evaluation / testing

- **What:** New installed-testing tier — `local-llm-installed-testing-design.md` codifies seven test levels (`static/unit/contract/package/install/runtime-local/live`) and adds `scripts/install-test-vault-local-llm.sh` (documented in `docs/reference/installer.md` "Disposable local-LLM install smoke"). `install` proves a fresh disposable vault + golden-copy restore against an Ollama/OpenAI-compatible endpoint (`memoria-qwen2.5:7b-64k`); `runtime-local` proves installed CLI dispatch reaches the local LLM, forbidden direct writes fail closed, and audit rows carry a task id — without requiring Hermes, Obsidian, or external providers. — **Why:** the design's Goal: "Prove Memoria works as an installed CLI system without making normal PRs depend on Ollama, Obsidian, or external providers." Nightly/RC-only cadence so the fast source gate is unchanged; "runtime-local proves wiring and policy behavior, not output quality" (do not assert generated prose). Commit `1ddcb624` "test: add local llm install smoke."

- **What:** `ai-catalog.json` regenerated with the new `enrich-source` capability entry (allowed_network Crossref/OpenAlex/Unpaywall, allowed_paths `.memoria/blobs/`, `inbox/`, `references.bib`; `provider_fetch`+`projection_writer` tools) and updated `capture-source`/`compile-source-digest` paths + trust hashes; `regenerate-references-bib` description now "from checked SQLite catalog rows" and retagged `alpha11→alpha12`. Tracked-projection drift check now "covers all committed projections, including the capability catalog" (`system-artifacts.md`). — **Why:** design §8/§10 "keep the tracked/shipped `capabilities/ai-catalog.json`"; §9 gate "`regenerate-tracked-projections` still includes `capabilities/ai-catalog.json`." The catalog is the tamper-evident capability manifest, so the new operation must appear with its trust hash.

- **What (fixes):** cron reliability — `cron-runner.sh` now exports `PYTHONPATH="$vault/.memoria:$vault/.memoria/mcp"`, and the release adds detection of paused Hermes cron jobs (commit `1ddcb624`). — **Why:** commit body: "fix: set cron runner python path" and "fix: detect paused Hermes cron jobs" — installed-vault cron workers were failing to import vault-local modules and paused jobs went unnoticed; surfaced by the new installed-testing gate.

### Profiles / runtime / naming alignment

- **What:** CLI-first / SSOT documentation reset — README/CHANGELOG/CITATION alpha source-install wording aligned, Hermes de-emphasized as the primary runtime, glossary reworded (background agents "execute board cards in lanes"; active lanes now `catalog/extract/link/map/verify` with Writer/`draft` and Engineer/`code` deferred; "Workspace" retagged alpha.11→alpha.12; `check_status` no longer "alpha.11"), and `set-up-zotero.md`/`integrations.md` updated so enrichment "calls Crossref, OpenAlex, and Unpaywall" reading `OPENALEX_API_KEY`+`NCBI_EMAIL`, with Semantic Scholar/PubMed marked deferred. — **Why:** cli-first-ssot-exec-plan §1: land "the smallest coherent pivot" so "current docs describe only implemented behavior; forward-looking decisions live in ADRs or scratch plans." Commits `517f556f` "docs: align root repo guidance," `5e54658a`, `00133616`, `b6f4e2ca`, `2e9bc2a5`.

### ADRs

- **What:** New **ADR-122 "SQLite working state and catalog records sit behind the checked Concept boundary"** (`assumes [28,55,119,121]`, `supersedes [49]`). Runtime working state + catalog record state live in `.memoria/state/memoria.sqlite`; the DB is *not* a second live Concept store; Bases become a view/projection layer, not catalog authority; PI mutation stays enqueue-only (ADR-121), and CLI is inspect/verify/administer only, "not a PI action surface." — **Why:** Context: the alpha.12 worker "needs indexed catalog rows for materialization, idempotency, bibliography rendering, and later provider provenance, while Bases are only a view layer" — ADR-49's catalog-frontmatter-as-SSOT "is now too strong." Rejected alternatives: JSON queue files as SSOT (strandable), catalog markdown as SSOT (couples worker state to Obsidian-shaped files), promoting SQLite to the canonical Concept store (opaque to Obsidian/Git). This is the decision-authority prerequisite the cli-first plan required before relying on new behavior.

- **What:** New **ADR-123 "DOI catalog enrichment gates checked source promotion"** (`assumes [30,32,57,119,121,122]`) — codifies the capture/enrich split, the `providers.yaml` + manifest-allowlist enforcement boundary, blob caching, provenance rows, the retraction/conflict gate, `inbox/` attention, and post-pass `references.bib` materialization; scopes the MVP to DOI only. — **Why:** turns design §8 decisions into an accepted decision record; alternatives rejected are the same four from the design (immediate promotion, staging markdown, all-providers-required, CLI/DB PI edit path). Enumerates its own implementation files and contract tests (`tests/test_alpha13_enrichment.py`).

- **What:** **ADR-49 marked `superseded → ADR-122`** (`docs/adr/49-…`, README index) with an inline supersession banner; its `assumes` flipped `[47]→[119]`. — **Why:** ADR-122 Consequence: "ADR-49's catalog-frontmatter source-of-truth decision is superseded. Bases may still render catalog-shaped views … but they are projections/fallbacks, not the catalog authority."

- **What:** **ADR-119 rewritten** from "the type schema is the complete declarative contract that validates, generates, and is the single source" to **"Concept schemas own field, home, read-state, and form contracts"** (~250 lines cut/rewritten; `assumes [52,116]`). Names four contract owners (type-schema YAML, `folders.yaml`, `check_status` read-state, Modal Forms as UI-only), pins the alpha.12 Concept roster, declares inbox cards as projections (not Concepts), and says project theses need no dedicated type. — **Why:** Context: the document contract "used to be split across ADR prose, schema YAML, folder maps, templates, Modal Forms, and hand-coded detectors … old decisions about type names, lifecycle values, forms, and folder homes drift after the alpha.12 schema simplification." Consolidating the contract is what let the 10 pre-reset ADRs below be retired without losing the decision. `frontmatter.md` correspondingly drops the `scripts/gen-forms.py` authority claim.

### Removed / retired

- **What:** Ten pre-reset ADRs deleted outright (files removed, dropped from `README.md` index) in commit `0851bb0e`: **39** note-acceptance checklists, **47** type-first category folders, **50** universal lifecycle & maturity, **51** inbox category & honesty card, **70** navigation gates/dashboards, **71** structured capture forms, **78** thesis note type, **81** persistent gate dashboards, **89** learning-to-rank triage, **117** kind-scoped type-naming scheme. — **Why:** these described the pre-alpha.11 typed-document / folder-taxonomy / dashboard / capture-form design that the alpha.11–12 reset replaced (ADR-114 navigator, 115 inbox-queue, 116 Obsidian-surface, 118 dashboard-consolidation, 119 schema-driven Concepts). Under the CLI-first-SSOT principle "current docs describe only implemented behavior; forward-looking decisions live in ADRs," keeping `accepted`-status ADRs that contradict the shipped model is drift; downstream references (`on-disk-layout.md`, others) were repointed from ADR-47/49/50 to ADR-116/119. *(Why for deletion-vs-supersede is inferred from the cli-first plan's decision-authority intent; the commit body itself is just the PR title.)*

- **What:** Stale catalog-ADR references cleaned across docs (commit `8836a4bf`, "retire stale catalog ADR") — `dashboards.md`, `linter.md`, `on-disk-layout.md`, `why-hermes.md`, `interaction-channels.md`, `vault.md`, and ~15 ADR cross-links repointed off ADR-49 onto ADR-116/119/122. — **Why:** consistency follow-through on the ADR-49 supersession so no shipped doc still cites catalog frontmatter as the source of truth.

- **What (retired code path, not deleted):** the alpha.12 behavior where `capture-source` promotes a scholarly DOI to `checked` is removed from the DOI/ISBN path (now stages unchecked); the direct `capture_source()` helper survives only for "already-supplied non-enrichment source payloads" (`ingest.md`, `capture.py`). — **Why:** design §1 "Do not let alpha.12 `capture_source()` promote a scholarly DOI/ISBN source to checked before alpha.13 enrichment"; ADR-123 core decision.

## alpha.14 — The standalone CLI + engine cut

**Theme: Memoria stops being an Obsidian/Hermes/Zotero/MCP/profile assembly and becomes one standalone `memoria` CLI over a SQLite engine, then builds out the DOI→OpenAlex/Crossref graph, full-text acquisition, gap/discovery, and universal Concept frontmatter on top of it.**

Alpha.14 is a full architecture cut, not a partial phase. The alpha.12 SQLite working-state boundary (ADR-122) and alpha.13 DOI enrichment (ADR-123) had already landed, so the engine existed; this release reconciles the surface/runtime drift by declaring the CLI+engine the product boundary and *dropping* — not deferring — Obsidian, Zotero, Hermes, MCP, installed profiles, lane/fleet, and `direct_api` as a product runner (`0.1.0-alpha.14-design.md` §0, §7; `0.1.0-alpha.14-release-plan.md` Status). The commit range splits into two waves: a foundational cutover (CLI spine #1045–#1053, runtime port #1114–#1121, dropped-surface sweep + `rg` negative gate #1118–#1130) and a change-heavy feature wave (#1131–#1157) that fills the graph-import, full-text, gap/discovery, retrieval, and frontmatter holes the cut opened. There is no production vault, so there is deliberately **no backward-compatibility mode, no migration path, and no legacy runtime branch** (`design.md` §0 Cutover rule).

---

### Vault / Concepts

- **What:** Universal Concept frontmatter is now *enforced* for every file under `knowledge/` and `capabilities/`: each Concept must carry `id` (= its bundle-relative path without `.md`), an approved `standing` (`current|superseded|retracted|archived`), and a map-shaped `links: {}` (new `apply_universal_concept_frontmatter` / `universal_concept_frontmatter_errors` in `src/memoria_vault/runtime/vaultio.py`; `UNIVERSAL_CONCEPT_BUNDLES={knowledge,capabilities}`). Trusted-writer validation and `note capture` now default and check these; shipped operation manifests, type schemas, and PI templates were backfilled (commit `88b7f0f5` / PR #1157; `trusted_writer.py`, `subsystems/lib/schema.py`, `vault-template/.memoria/schemas/types/{digest,hub,adapter}.yaml`, every `capabilities/operations/*.md`). **Why:** `knowledge/` and `capabilities/` are declared OKF Knowledge Bundles where "a Concept ID is the path without `.md`" and "every Concept is YAML frontmatter followed by a Markdown body" (`design.md` §3 OKF bundle contract, §12 "Universal Concept frontmatter … `id`, `standing`, and map-shaped `links`"). Without enforcement, `standing`-based supersession filtering (§10 retrieval hides superseded/retracted) and map-shaped `links` graph traversal have no guaranteed field to read; the gate §14 explicitly requires "Universal Concept frontmatter requires `id`, `standing`, and map-shaped `links`."

- **What:** Type schemas were tightened to make the universal fields *required* rather than optional and to add the `standing` enum. In `digest.yaml`/`hub.yaml`, `id: str`, `standing: enum:standing`, and `links: map` moved into `required:`, and `links` was removed from `optional:` (was `links: list`), i.e. links became a map not a list (`88b7f0f5`). **Why:** the alpha.13 object model carried `links` as an ad-hoc optional list; alpha.14's model (`design.md` §4) makes `links: {}` a typed map on the frontmatter baseline so machine graph reads are shape-stable, and makes `standing` first-class so lint can surface superseded/retracted evidence (§9 check surface: "stale-as-current evidence, retraction/contested evidence").

- **What:** New tracked generated projection `knowledge/_views/index.md` — a worker-owned "Knowledge views index" carrying a `Generated by memoria_vault.runtime.projections; edit source Concepts instead` banner (PR #1156 `f9e56093`; `runtime/projections.py`, `vault-template/knowledge/_views/index.md`). It was wired into projection drift checks, direct-write scan quarantine, `init --dry-run` targets, runtime replay, package refresh, and shipped template evidence. **Why:** `status --json` and generated `knowledge/_views/` replace the retired dashboard glance surfaces (`design.md` §5 "Generated views under `knowledge/_views/` cover daily glance, structural health, operational health, and synthesis agenda as files, not UI cards"); §14 gate requires "`workspace rebuild` emits final generated paths: `knowledge/index.md`, `capabilities/index.md`, `knowledge/_views/`." Making it a *tracked* worker-owned projection means a direct editor write to it is a foreign write that must quarantine (§2 foreign-write classification), which the PR also proved.

- **What:** Concept object model is now records-vs-Concepts-vs-projections with **no markdown Work/Author/Source/Institution Concepts** at all — Works, Authors, OpenAlex Sources, Institutions, Topics, Publishers, Funders, and graph links are SQLite rows; a Work's only keep-set presence is its digest (`design.md` §3–§4). The legacy markdown Work source fallback was removed from digest, integrity, rollback, projection, and seeded-error paths (PR #1121 `ace45000`), and a `workspace check --assert no-legacy-work-markdown` assertion plus CLI test was added (`d55fb98f`). **Why:** carries forward alpha.13's clean boundary (§4, ADR reference); the design forbids legacy markdown Work lookup in the runtime (§12 "Dropped: Legacy markdown Work lookup or schema support") and §14 requires "Lookup, digest, references, attention, rollback, and recovery work by `work_id` without a legacy markdown Work path." Checked SQLite catalog rows plus blob content are now the sole source authority (ADR-124).

- **What:** Retired the shipped Obsidian workspace payload from `vault-template`: the entire `.obsidian/**` tree, QuickAdd command scripts/buttons, and the plugin provenance lock, plus the JS helper scripts `capture-note.js`, `open-inbox.js`, `quickadd-utils.js`, `record-exploration-trace.js`, `resolve-inbox-card.js`, `restore-memoria-shell.js` (PR #1124 `5a93b142`). **Why:** Obsidian is dropped as a required surface (`design.md` §0, §13 Non-goals); the parity table (§5) re-homes every palette action to a CLI command (`Memoria: capture note`→`memoria note capture`, `open Inbox`→`attention list`, `record exploration trace`→`project trace`, `resolve/dismiss inbox card`→`attention resolve --outcome`, and "restore shell on startup" becomes adapter-only, not core). The product "must remain fully operable if the editor is only `vim`, `nano`, or a file browser" (§1).

---

### Profiles / Runtime

- **What:** New grouped `memoria <resource> <action>` console script — the entire ~2274-line `src/memoria_vault/cli.py` is new (CLI spine #1045 `9e8a4c8b`; command surface wired across #1046–#1053). It implements the resource-oriented grammar with global `--workspace/--json/--quiet/--verbose/--yes/--dry-run/--idempotency-key/--schedule-id` options and the full command roster (`init`, `status`, `doctor`, `ask`, `work capture|import|enrich|digest|interview|update`, `note capture|propose|accept|reject|link`, `project ask|trace|gaps|suggest-hubs|export`, `request answer|amend|cancel|retry|resume|list|show`, `attention …`, `operation list|run`, `steering …`, `vocabulary …`, `journal …`, `workspace scan|run|recover|rollback|check|rebuild|export`, `eval …`). A test pins the exact command roster (`6b1c82cf`). **Why:** "The engine is the product boundary. All surfaces create the same request envelope" (`design.md` §2); the CLI is "the product surface for alpha.14," not operator-only (§5). `--workspace` not `--vault` because "alpha.14 is a standalone workspace, not an Obsidian vault adapter" (§5). The stale `project create` command was removed because projects are authored as checked Markdown then scanned, not minted by a command (`6b1c82cf` body).

- **What:** Request envelope aligned to the alpha.14 minimum shape (`request_id`, `operation_id`, `args`, `idempotency_key`, `actor`, `input_refs[]`, `output_intents[]`, `primary_target?`, `precondition_hashes{}`, `causal_refs[]`, `provenance`, `schedule_id?`) with **no dedicated ingress-type field** (#1053 `202e9166`; envelope kept in sync across `args_json`/job payload/`request_envelope.args` in #1132 `06063b29`). A `cancelled` request status was added (#1054 `ff02e879`), and `request retry` was restricted to replay only when idempotency key/inputs/precondition hashes still match (#1058 `996d6bed`). **Why:** work enters exactly three ways (CLI, scan-observed file change, scheduled task) and "the command name, actor, provenance, and optional `schedule_id` are enough" — an ingress-type field would be redundant state (`design.md` §2, §14 "The request envelope has no dedicated ingress-type field"). `output_intents[]` replaces alpha.13's `output_target` so no prompt operation owns a canonical write path (§4). Envelope-sync avoids divergent copies of the args that audit and replay read.

- **What:** pydantic-ai is now the **sole** operation runner; Hermes-as-runtime/library and `direct_api` dispatch were removed, and all checked operation manifests declare `runner: pydantic-ai` (e.g. `analyze-gaps.md` `runner: local`→`runner: pydantic-ai`). Legacy operation runners were dropped (#1056 `dac5570d`), prompt operations run through the worker (#1094 `c7ccfd49`), a default local runner endpoint was set (#1087 `b5b1ff99`), and the runner is proven in `doctor` (#1079 `ef1e0caa`). **Why:** the runner is "a Memoria implementation detail" with pydantic-ai for typed LLM calls, structured output, and retries over an OpenAI-compatible endpoint; Hermes runtime/library, LangChain/LlamaIndex framework-owned state, and workflow engines are "Rejected as baseline" (`design.md` §7). `direct_api` "does not stay as a competing product runner" (§12). "No competing product paths" (§0).

- **What:** All 26 legacy `.memoria/operations/` Python modules were ported into `src/memoria_vault/runtime/subsystems/` before their old homes were deleted — ingest (`processing/ingest/{classify,extract,ingest_paper,link,resolve_merge,resolve_merge_logic,resolve_merge_pubmed,runner}.py`), cleanup (`cleanup/reconcile.py`), integrity linter (`integrity/linter/{detectors,detectors_audit,detectors_design,golden_restore,hub_handoff,precommit_check,session_summary}.py`), retraction (`integrity/retraction/retraction.py`), project structural-impact (`processing/project/structural_impact{,_graph}.py`), eval (`telemetry/eval/{eval_dispatch,eval_score}.py`), and shared libs (`lib/{inbox,loudness,markdown,schema,worklists}.py`) (PR #1117 `4fca09d8`, home deleted #1118 `0ac33690`). **Why:** "Existing operation implementations are import inputs, not disposable history … No old operation is deleted just because its old host was Hermes/MCP/profile-shaped" (`design.md` §5). Import means the behavior runs through the request envelope, file capability manifests, and SQLite state — preserving the linter finding classes, retraction logic, ingest/merge, and worklist shapes (§12 "ported as CLI/report contracts").

- **What:** The `mcp` capability type was renamed to `adapter` (optional `capabilities/adapters/<id>.md` Concepts); `mcp` is no longer a capability type (#1116 `6ba172b0`; `adapter.yaml` schema). Policy-hook enforcement moved into `src/memoria_vault/runtime/policy/` (`policy/hook.py`, `policy/workspace.py`) and the shipped `.memoria/mcp/` adapter home was removed (#1120 `f7628337`). **Why:** MCP is dropped as a required operation API; adapters may exist "later only as optional adapters around the CLI/engine," and "No external adapter ever owns state, workflow, policy, checks, or the write boundary" (`design.md` §0, §4 "Current code/docs name the equivalent type `mcp`; alpha.14 must either rename it, drop it, or keep it only as an optional adapter Concept").

- **What:** Installed profiles and the lane/fleet runtime model were removed wholesale: shipped profiles, lane overrides, the profile tool registry, profile rendering, live Hermes/L2 smoke scripts, and profile/Hermes installer modes (#1119 `a3794fb6`); the runtime lane-policy loader was replaced with actor/workspace policy loaded from `<workspace>/.memoria/config/policy.yaml` (`policy/lanes.py` deleted, #1126 `102e0204`); remaining non-policy `lane`/`task_id` residue was purged — work-prompt metadata now uses `request_id` + optional `posture`, eval routing uses `eval_role`, and the shipped Hermes-backed `.githooks/post-commit` trigger was deleted (#1128 `aa6a7a56`). `session_id` is no longer accepted as a request-id fallback. **Why:** installed profiles and lane/fleet are "dropped, not deferred" (`design.md` §0); the runner rejects "Agent session memory as authority" and "co-trained generator+reviewer … confidence-routed bypass of the human checkpoint" (§7). Actor+`request_id` audit pairing is the standalone control-plane equivalent (§9, ADR reference). See `docs/design/why-not-autonomous.md` lineage for rejecting profile/lane autonomy.

- **What:** Worker requests are now SQLite-only (#1059 `5df4f73f`), the runtime state layout was aligned (#1060 `b288d413`), and a schema-migration shim was removed (#1057 `d95f7cb4`). **Why:** SQLite is the authority for graph/ops/queue/journal/checks/rollback (`design.md` §0, §3); with no production vault there is no migration target, so the shim is dead machinery (§0 "no migration path … Existing compatibility code, tests, docs, and schema paths are removed").

---

### Gate / Provenance / Integrity

- **What:** `workspace scan` now records `observed_external_edit` journal events and reports observed PI edits that "need checking" in `workspace scan --json`; a direct edit to a checked keep-set Concept is marked `unchecked`/non-consumable and re-promoted only through the `mark-checked` capability (not a new top-level command) (#1055 `6a3ab4bc`, #1133 `fa569367`; projections regenerated after quarantine #1088 `a1887e7c`). A change to a generated projection, worker-owned path, `references.bib`, or capability manifest is *quarantined*, never re-consumed, proven by a `direct-write-generated-projection` fixture (#1084 `7d7f1878`). **Why:** `workspace scan` is "the only bridge for direct editor/file-browser edits" and foreign-write classification imports a keep-set edit as a PI edit (preserving prior upstream inputs + prior checked hash for cascade rollback) but quarantines anything worker-owned (`design.md` §2). §14 gate: "an edit to a generated projection, worker-owned path, `references.bib`, or capability manifest is quarantined, not consumed." This is the structural read-barrier substitute for per-write approval (`why-review-gate-is-structural.md` lineage).

- **What:** New **live-runner proof gate**: `memoria doctor --check runner --live` performs an opt-in real pydantic-ai dispatch through the same model/network policy guard operations use, and `scripts/verify live` runs the live pytest marker (#1145 `1341786d`; `test_live_runner.py`). **Why:** "The local-runner check is explicit because a deterministic digest fixture does not prove model dispatch" (`design.md` §11); §14 gate: "Runtime-local installed gate proves local runner dispatch with an explicit `doctor --check runner` check; deterministic digest fixtures do not count as runner proof." Deterministic fixtures let the whole loop pass without any model ever being called, which would be a false green.

- **What:** New **runtime replay gate**: a focused `test_alpha14_runtime_gate.py` (462 lines) exercises the full alpha.14 command sequence (init→capture→enrich→update→interview→digest→note curation→recovery→runner/qmd doctors→scan quarantine→scheduled queue/check→rebuild→ask/project ask/export→journal→seeded-error verdict), and `scripts/verify runtime` runs it before the older runtime suites (#1134 `724e6927`). **Why:** "the alpha.14 product loop is complete only when the CLI can run a thin end-to-end cycle" (`design.md` §5); the runtime-local gate (§11) must prove installed CLI wiring, write boundary, denied direct write, audit rows, recovery, and the seeded-error verdict before any non-sandbox use, using checked-in provider-replay and crash fixtures so it "does not depend on external providers or timing."

- **What:** The seeded-error verdict is wired as a first-class CLI gate (`memoria eval seeded-error-verdict`, #1048 `3ee961cc`; `seeded_errors.py` reworked, and `alpha11-`/`alpha12-seeded-errors.json` fixtures updated). Digest-journal operation aliases were mapped (#1086 `23f3cab0`) and a crash-before-materialization recovery fixture added (#1085 `22e7b27b`). **Why:** the seeded-error harness is "the gate to real use" — no structural check proves semantic truth (`design.md` §9). The provisional bars stand: 100% structural detection recall, 0 false-clean, ≤10% false-positive, 100% rollback completeness; and "The seeded-error harness measures the human checkpoint against a no-checkpoint baseline" (§9, §14) — a checkpoint that isn't measurably better than none "is theatre and gets thinned." This is the correctness-via-integrity bet from the literature review (FEVER evidence-grounded NLI, generator/verifier sample-and-rank; `_papers/REVIEW-REFUTATIONS.md`).

- **What:** Journal-list filters added (by request, path, decision, operation, date, check) (#1105 `31afb9d7`); `doctor --repair` restores missing/corrupt packaged capability/skeleton files, plain `doctor` only reports (#1104 `9719fe06`); `init --dry-run` report expanded to cover skeleton/DB/baseline/generated targets/steering/vocabulary/qmd collection/provider config (#1106 `12ca88a4`). **Why:** "The journal is forensic truth; `request show` and `journal show` are user-facing summaries over it" (`design.md` §9); `doctor` "checks local prerequisites and never repairs without an explicit flag" (§5), and repair "restores missing/corrupt packaged … files from the installed package baseline" (§11).

- **What:** Network allowlist matching was hardened so adapter HTTP bypassing the shared allowlist fails closed (#1103 `7c843f5d`). **Why:** "Every HTTP call passes a shared operation allowlist check before network I/O"; "the operation manifest is the hard ceiling for network access" (`design.md` §8); §9 security: "Network access is operation-scoped and allowlisted." §14 gate: "Adapter HTTP bypassing shared allowlist fails closed."

---

### Pipeline / Ingest / Enrichment

This is the change-heaviest area. The DOI→OpenAlex/Crossref graph and full-text acquisition were built out across #1135–#1155.

- **What:** Capture became **SQLite-only**: `capture_source`/`capture_bibtex_source`/`capture_url_source`/`capture_pdf_source` now stage into SQLite catalog rows plus `.memoria/blobs/source-content/<work-id>/…` payloads and no longer write legacy Work markdown, derived-entity markdown, or a capture-time `references.bib` (`runtime/capture.py` heavily reworked, #1110–#1114). `references.bib` and the capability index render from checked SQLite rows only (#1113 `26552935`). **Why:** capture "Stores raw/content hashes … Does not update `references.bib` … Does not create markdown Work, Author, OpenAlex Source, or Institution records" (`design.md` §8); `references.bib` is a generated projection from checked catalog rows, not a capture-time or user-maintained file (ADR-124 Consequences).

- **What:** Full-text is now **required before a checked digest**: metadata-only/abstract-only digest attempts fail in the shared runtime path, create a stable full-text attention projection, expose the attention path in the failed-request error, and leave no consumable digest output (#1068 `2e6e4315`, #1069 `59b5ceb1`, #1135 `49bae16e`; `flag digest without full text`). **Why:** decided policy: "a checked digest is compiled only from acquired full work text or a user-supplied equivalent. Abstracts and metadata … cannot produce a checked digest. Full-text acquisition is therefore baseline alpha.14 functionality, not a deferred enrichment" (`design.md` §8, resolved §15). §14 gate: "no checked digest is produced from abstract-only or metadata-only input."

- **What:** Open-Access full-text acquisition was made robust with an ordered candidate retry loop: try Unpaywall `best_oa_location`, then `oa_locations` (#1140 `229249ab`, #1141 `b9703650`), then OpenAlex `open_access.oa_url` / `best_oa_location` / `primary_location` / `locations` (#1144 `bf47fe5f`), then Crossref `message.link[].URL` (#1151 `62011e1c`) — each candidate URL/PEP passed through the same allowlist-before-I/O check, deduped, and skipped if denied/failed/extraction-failing/empty until one yields extractable text (#1070 `805bee06`). **Why:** because full text is now a hard digest precondition, a single dead OA URL cannot be allowed to block an otherwise-acquirable Work; the DOI-scholarly branch lists "Unpaywall/OA locator; acquired full text" as *required for checked promotion* (`design.md` §8 Branches). Paywalled bypass/credentialed scraping stays a non-goal (§13), so acquisition is limited to legal OA locations.

- **What:** First-order citation/reference/topic graph import was expanded far beyond alpha.13. During DOI enrichment Memoria now imports: reference edges from portable BibTeX/CSL metadata into `work_graph_edges` (#1139 `c172a0de`); OpenAlex `topics` + `primary_topic` (#1142 `d32dca03`), `concepts` as `topic` edges (#1149 `dedccea8`), `keywords` as `keyword` edges (#1143 `ef99b11f`), `mesh` and `sustainable_development_goals` as topic edges (#1155 `a618b1ed`), and `authorships` + nested institutions + location Source metadata as graph edges (#1154 `cf9f23ef`); plus Crossref `relation` rows as `related` edges (#1150 `c3538d47`). Discovered candidate Works are marked unchecked attention/worklist rows, never checked (`runtime/enrichment.py`). **Why:** enrichment "Imports the first-order citation/reference/topic graph available from required providers and marks discovered candidate Works as unchecked attention/worklist rows, not checked knowledge" (`design.md` §8); the graph feeds retrieval query expansion and gap analysis (§10 "First-order citation/reference graph, OpenAlex Topics, controlled facets … part of the read model"). Depth stays first-order by design — "Exhaustive or provider-specific graph expansion" is a non-goal (§13).

- **What:** Crossref full-text links are acquired and OA URLs preferred (#1144, #1151); enrichment tries fallback OA lists (#1140/#1141). qmd embedding-enabled rebuilds now persist `mode: hybrid`, `embeddings: true`, and the exact `qmd embed --chunk-strategy auto` command in the checked-search manifest (#1152 `e7e624ef`). **Why:** the DOI branch requires "embeddings" for checked promotion (`design.md` §8); recording the embedding manifest mode makes the retrieval build reproducible and gate-checkable (§10 rebuild contract).

- **What:** BibTeX/CSL portable imports stage as unchecked Work rows with queued enrichment (#1073 `e4476012`); the Zotero-specific import surface (CLI `--format zotero-export`, worker operation, runtime helper, capability file, `capture-zotero-source.md`, `regenerate-ai-catalog.md`) was removed (#1123 `7ad88a84`), though a Zotero *export file* still stages as an unchecked Work via generic import (#1077 `e3f10cad`). **Why:** "`work import --format zotero-export` is not preserved as a product alias. Portable bibliography import means generic BibTeX/CSL files only" (`design.md` §5, §8); Zotero is dropped as required Work authority (ADR-124: "Zotero and Better BibTeX are optional user tools … Memoria does not require a live Zotero library"). §14 gate: "`work import --format zotero-export` fails as an unsupported format."
